Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'face' in the hadith implies a physical face or body part for Allah.
Correction: The author explicitly interprets 'face' as the essence (dhāt), because a literal face or any limb is impossible for Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the 'lifting of the veil' (raf' al-hijāb) mean?
A) Removing a literal curtain so that Allah is seen with physical eyes
B) Removing the barrier from the eyes of the beholders and creating perceptions related to Allah's essence
C) Uncovering a hidden light
D) Opening the door of Paradise

Key Takeaway
The first hadith proof for the beatific vision is understood through the lens of tanzih: 'face' means essence, and the vision is a direct perception of Allah without corporeality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the hadith 'they look at the face of Allah,' what instinctive image comes to your mind? How does the author's explanation challenge that image, and what does that reveal about your own assumptions about Allah? Are you willing to let go of any anthropomorphic ideas you may be holding onto?
?
The hadith says that nothing was given to the people more beloved than the vision. If you truly believed that seeing Allah is the greatest gift, how would that change your priorities today? What are you currently seeking more than that vision, and will you reorder your life to make it your ultimate pursuit?
?
The author interprets 'lifting the veil' as Allah creating perceptions in you. Reflect: What barriers in your heart—such as arrogance, heedlessness, or love of this world—prevent you from perceiving Allah's presence now? What will you do today to ask Him to remove those barriers so that you can taste even a glimpse of knowing Him?

The Highest Rank: Second Hadith and Consensus
Author cites second hadith and consensus to reinforce the beatific vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second hadith about the ranks of Paradise and the consensus of the salaf further establish the reality of the vision of Allah while emphasizing its supreme honor.

Core Idea
The greatest gift in Paradise is seeing Allah's essence, and this truth is known by consensus from the earliest Muslims.

After explaining the first hadith, Imam Sanusi presents another prophetic narration that distinguishes the lowest and highest inhabitants of Paradise. The highest honor is looking at Allah's face morning and evening. The author again interprets 'face' as the essence. He then appeals to the consensus (ijmā') of the righteous predecessors (salaf) whose longing for the vision is well-known. This lesson covers these additional proofs and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the second hadith
Examine the hadith about the lowest and highest ranks of Paradise. Note the contrast between the extensive physical delights of the lowest and the vision of Allah's face for the highest.
The hadith emphasizes that the vision is the most honored gift.
2
Understand the author's gloss on 'face'
Sanusi again interprets 'face' as the essence, explicitly stating that a literal face or any limb is impossible for Allah.
This reinforces the same interpretive principle from lesson 1.
3
Appreciate the consensus argument
The author invokes the consensus of the righteous predecessors, whose known desire for the vision confirms its reality. Consider why consensus is a strong proof in Sunni theology.
The salaf's longing is taken as evidence that the vision is real and desirable.
4
Reflect on the concluding statement
Sanusi states that the reality of the vision is almost a necessary known of religion. Reflect on what this means: it is so well-established that denying it is nearly impossible for a Muslim.
This ties the proof to the concept of 'ilm darūrī (necessary knowledge).

Refuting the Claim of Contradiction in the Quran
Sanusi refutes the charge of contradiction in the Quran with two specific examples and their reconciliations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how apparent contradictions in the Quran are resolved by denying the conditions of contradiction and providing contextual reconciliations, as exemplified by the verses about questioning and the foods of Hell.

Core Idea
Quranic apparent contradictions dissolve when we examine context and intended meanings.

Sanusi addresses a serious objection: that the Quran contradicts itself. He begins with a firm refutation, then shows that the alleged contradictions are not true contradictions because the conditions are not met. He then provides detailed reconciliations for two pairs of verses, demonstrating the proper method of tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the two pairs of verses cited by the critics and see why they appear to conflict: the questioning verses and the food verses.
2
Grasp the general response
Sanusi denies that the conditions for contradiction exist, pointing to detailed explanations in tafsir works.
The conditions of contradiction are clearly defined in logic.
3
Examine the first reconciliation
The two questioning verses are reconciled by distinguishing between questioning for rebuke (توبيخ) and questioning for information (استعلام). The latter is impossible for Allah.
4
Examine the second reconciliation
The two foods (ضريع and غسلين) are either for different groups in Hell or are the same thing, removing the conflict.
Scholars differ on whether they are synonyms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رد شبهة أنَّ فيه تناقضاً
ومنها : أن قالوا شتَّتَ اللهُ تعالى شملهم ، وهَدَمَ أُشُهُم [؟] ، وأبطل حراكهم وحِسَّهم : إِنَّ فِيهِ تناقضاً ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ فَيَوْمَئِذٍ لَا يُسْأَلُ عَنْ ذَنْبِهِ إنس ولا جان ﴾ [الرحمن : ٣٩]، مع قوله تعالى : ﴿ فَوَرَبِّكَ لَنَسْأَلَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ * عَمَّا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الحجر : ۹۲-۹۳) ، وكقوله تعالى : ﴿ لَيْسَ لَهُمْ طَعَامُ إِلَّا مِنْ ضَرِيعٍ ﴾ [الغاشية : ٦]، مع قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَلَا طَعَامُ إِلَّا مِنْ غِسْلِينِ ﴾ [الحاقة : ١٣٦]، إلى غير ذلك مِنْ مواضع يُتوهَّمُ فيها تنافي الكلامين .
والرد عليهم : بمنع وجودِ شرائط التناقض ، وقد بُيِّنَ ذلك على التفصيل التام في كتب التفسير .
فأحد ما قيل في الجمع بين الآيتين السابقتين : أنَّ السؤال المثبت هو سؤال التوبيخ والإيقاف على خبائث الأعمال ، والسؤال المنفي هو سؤال الاستعلام والاستخبارِ ، ولا شكّ أنَّهُ مستحيل على الله تعالى ؛ لأنَّه العالم بكل شيء .
وأحد ما قيل في الجمع بين الأخيرتين بناء على أنَّ الغسلينَ مباين في المعنى للضريع ، وأنَّ الغِسلين صديد أهل النار وما يجري مِنْ جراحهم ، والضريع شجرةُ الزَّقُوم ، أو شوك فيها ، أو نبت فيها : أنَّ الغِسلينَ طعام لقوم لا يأكلون غيرَهُ ، والضريع طعام لقوم آخرين لا يأكلون غيرَهُ ، وأمَّا مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّ الضريعَ والغسلينَ بمعنى واحدٍ ، والغسلين يجري مِنَ الضريع .. فلا إشكال حينئذ .
Refutation of the suspicion that there is contradiction in it. Among them: that they said – may Allah scatter them, destroy their nests, and nullify their movement and perception – "Indeed in it there is contradiction"; like His statement (Surah Ar-Rahman 55:39): "Then on that Day, no man or jinn will be asked about his sin" along with His statement (Surah Al-Hijr 15:92-93): "But by your Lord, We will surely ask them all about what they used to do." And like His statement (Surah Al-Ghashiyah 88:6): "They have no food except from thorny plants" along with His statement (Surah Al-Haqqah 69:36): "And no food except from filth." And other places where conflict between two statements is imagined. And the response to them: by denying the existence of the conditions of contradiction, and that has been explained in full detail in books of tafsir. Among what has been said in reconciling the two preceding verses: that the affirmed questioning is the questioning of rebuke and exposure of evil deeds, and the negated questioning is the questioning of inquiry and seeking information, and there is no doubt that that is impossible for Allah, for He is the Knower of all things. And among what has been said in reconciling the latter two, based on the fact that 'ghislin' (filth) is different in meaning from 'dari'' (thorny plant), and that 'ghislin' is the pus of the people of Hell and what flows from their wounds, and 'dari'' is the tree of Zaqqum, or thorns in it, or a plant in it: that 'ghislin' is food for a people who eat nothing else, and 'dari'' is food for another people who eat nothing else. And as for whoever said that 'dari'' and 'ghislin' are one meaning, and that 'ghislin' flows from 'dari'' – then there is no problem at that point.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. It first presents the objectors' claim that the Quran contains contradictions, citing two pairs of verses: (1) the denial of questioning on the Day of Judgment and the affirmation of questioning, and (2) the mention of two different foods for the people of Hell (ضريع and غسلين). The response immediately denies that the conditions for contradiction are met, referring to detailed explanations in tafsir works. Then it provides specific reconciliations. For the first pair, the two types of questioning are distinguished: the negated questioning is one of inquiry (استعلام) – impossible for the All-Knowing – while the affirmed questioning is one of rebuke (توبيخ). For the second pair, one interpretation holds that the two foods are for different groups in Hell, so no contradiction; another interpretation holds that they are the same thing, which also removes the contradiction.

Key Terms
تناقض
شرائط التناقض
توبيخ
استعلام
ضريع
غسلين
صديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That apparent textual contradictions in the Quran constitute actual logical contradictions without considering context or the conditions for genuine contradiction.
Correction: Apparent contradictions are resolved by considering the context, the conditions for contradiction, and multiple possible interpretations as shown in tafsir.

Checkpoint
How do the reconciliations resolve the apparent contradiction between the verses about questioning?
A) By denying that the verses are authentic.
B) By distinguishing between questioning of rebuke and questioning for information.
C) By claiming the first verse is abrogated.
D) By interpreting both verses metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in the Quran are resolved by examining context and distinguishing between different meanings, not by denying authenticity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a verse of the Quran that seems difficult or contradictory to another, do you immediately doubt the Quran or do you seek deeper understanding as this lesson teaches? What is the state of your heart when you encounter such verses, and what can you do today to strengthen your trust in Allah's perfect speech?
?
The lesson shows that Allah's questioning on the Day of Judgment is not to seek information but to rebuke. How does knowing that Allah already knows everything about you change the way you think about being held accountable? Are you preparing for that moment of exposure, or are you hiding from it?
?
The reconciliations in this lesson required effort and knowledge of Arabic and tafsir. Are you willing to invest time in learning your religion deeply so that you can defend the Quran against doubts? What specific step will you take this week to increase your understanding of controversial or difficult passages?

Refuting the Claim of Falsehood in the Quran
Sanusi refutes the objection by offering two interpretations of the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that the Quran contains falsehood by offering two interpretations that resolve the apparent chronological inconsistency in al-A'raf 7:11.

Core Idea
The Quran is free from falsehood; apparent contradictions are resolved through metaphor or context.

This lesson examines a common objection raised against the Quran: that it contains falsehood because of an apparent chronological inconsistency in verse 7:11. Sanusi presents the objection and then provides two compelling interpretations that show the verse is truthful. By studying this passage, you will learn how classical scholars defend the Quran's integrity using sound linguistic and theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. The objectors claim that verse 7:11 is false because the command to prostrate to Adam came before the creation of humanity.
Note the phrase 'لِلْقَطْعِ بِأَنَّ الْأَمْرَ بِالسُّجُودِ لَمْ يَكُنْ بَعْدَ خَلْقِنَا وَتَصْوِيرِنَا'.
2
First interpretation – metaphorical
Sanusi explains that 'you' in the verse refers to Adam as our origin. The creation of Adam is attributed to us metaphorically, similar to saying 'I planted this crop' when one planted the seed.
This is a common Arabic usage (مجاز مشهور).
3
Second interpretation – literal
Another interpretation is that 'creation' refers to the extraction of Adam's offspring (الذر) from his back before the prostration command. This makes the verse literal and the chronology correct.
Here the verse is 'عَلَى ظَاهِرِهَا' without forced interpretation.
4
Reflect on the defense
Why do both interpretations succeed? Notice how scholars use linguistic analysis (metaphor) and contextual knowledge (the ذر narrative) to defend the Quran's truthfulness.
This shows the depth of Quranic exegesis and the importance of understanding Arabic rhetoric.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رد شبهة أنَّ فيه كذباً
ومنها : أنْ قالوا لعنَهُمُ اللهُ : إِنَّ فيه الكذبَ المحْضَ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ( وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ صَوَّرْنَاكُمْ ثُمَّ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَائِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لِآدَمَ ) [الأعراف : ١١] للقطع بأنَّ الأمر بالسجودِ لم يكن بعد خلقنا وتصويرنا .
والرد عليهم : بأنَّ المراد خَلْقُ أبينا آدم عليه الصلاة والسلامُ وتصويره ، ولمَّا كانَ أصلنا هو الذي أنشأنا الله سبحانَهُ منه ، ونحنُ جزء منه . . جعل سبحانه خلقه وتصويره كأنَّهُ خَلْقُ وتصوير لنا ، فعدد سبحانه نعمه علينا ؛ إذْ شَرَّفَنا جلَّ وعزَّ بمحْض فضله بإسجاد الملائكة الكرام لأبينا ، وتشريف الأب تشريف لولده .
ومثل هذا المجازِ مشهورٌ ؛ يقولُ أحدنا : زرعتُ هذا الزرع ، والمراد : أَنَّهُ زرعَ أصلَهُ الذي أنشَأهُ اللهُ تعالى منه ، وكذا : زرعتُ هذهِ النخلةَ ، والمراد : أَنَّهُ زرع أصلها الذي هو النوى .
وقيل : المراد بالخَلْقِ والتصوير السابقين على الأمر بالسجودِ : خَلْقُ ذُرِّيَّةِ آدم وتصويرهم أولاً حينَ أُخْرِجُوا مِنْ أبيهم آدمَ كَالذَّرِّ ؛ إذْ ثبت أنَّه بعد إخراجهم مِنْ أبيهم وتصويرهم حينئذٍ أمر الملائكة بالسجود لآدم عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ، فصارَتْ الآية على هذا التأويل على ظاهرها ، لا يُحتاجُ إلى تكلُّف تأويل ، فأي شيء يشكلُ مِنْ هذا لولا الجهلُ وعمى البصيرة ؟! ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله ، نسأله سبحانه العافية في الدارين بمنّه
Refutation of the suspicion that there is falsehood in it. Among them: that they said – may Allah curse them – "Indeed in it is pure falsehood"; like His statement (Surah Al-A'raf 7:11): "And We created you, then We formed you, then We said to the angels: 'Prostrate to Adam'" – because it is certain that the command to prostrate was not after our creation and formation. And the response to them: that what is meant is the creation and formation of our father Adam (peace be upon him), and since our origin is that from which Allah (glorified be He) created us, and we are a part of him, He (glorified be He) made His creation and formation of him as if it were creation and formation of us. So He enumerated His blessings upon us, since He honored us (majestic and exalted) by pure virtue through the prostration of the noble angels to our father, and honoring the father is honoring his children. And this kind of metaphor is well-known; one of us says: "I planted this crop", meaning that he planted its origin which Allah created, and similarly: "I planted this palm tree", meaning that he planted its origin, which is the seed. And it was said: what is meant by the creation and formation that precede the command to prostrate is the creation and formation of Adam's offspring first, when they were taken out from their father Adam like tiny ants (dharr); since it is established that after their extraction from their father and their formation at that time, He commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam (peace be upon him). So the verse, according to this interpretation, is in its apparent meaning, without need for forced interpretation. So what is difficult in this except ignorance and blindness of insight?! There is no power or strength except with Allah. We ask Him (glorified be He) for well-being in both abodes by His grace.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. It first presents the objectors' claim that the Quran contains falsehood, citing the verse that says 'We created you, then formed you, then said to the angels: prostrate to Adam' – noting that the command to prostrate occurred before the creation of humans, so the sequence seems false. The response offers two interpretations. First: the verse is metaphorical – 'you' refers to Adam as our origin, so creation and formation of Adam is considered as ours by synecdoche (part for whole). This is supported by common Arabic usage, e.g., 'I planted this crop' meaning the seed. Second: the verse is literal but refers to the creation of Adam's offspring (the ذر) from his back before the command to prostrate, so the order is correct. Both interpretations vindicate the verse from falsehood.

Key Terms
كذب
مجاز
إسجاد
ذر
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quran contains falsehood due to an apparent chronological inconsistency in verse 7:11.
Correction: The verse is not false; it can be understood metaphorically (Adam as origin) or as referring to the creation of Adam's offspring before the prostration command.

Checkpoint
What is one interpretation given to reconcile the verse about creation and prostration?
A) The verse refers to Adam as the origin of humanity, so it is metaphorical.
B) The verse is abrogated by another verse.
C) The word 'you' refers to the angels.
D) The command to prostrate occurred after the creation of humans.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is truthful; apparent chronological issues are resolved through metaphor or contextual interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse that seems contradictory to other knowledge, is your first reaction to doubt the Quran or to seek deeper understanding? What does that reveal about the state of your iman?
?
Sanusi uses a common Arabic metaphor (planting a crop) to explain the verse. Do you accept that the Quran uses figurative language? How does that affect your trust in its literal truth?
?
If someone presented this objection to you today, would you be able to defend the Quran's truthfulness with the arguments from this lesson? What does your answer say about your responsibility to learn and convey these defenses?

The Prophet's Renunciation: Three Hadiths
Sanusi cites three hadith variants illustrating the Prophet's renunciation of the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three prophetic hadiths from different contexts collectively teach the virtue of renouncing worldly attachments.

Core Idea
The Prophet chose poverty over gold to teach us detachment.

Sanusi brings together three hadiths that illustrate the Prophet's voluntary renunciation of worldly wealth and status. Each hadith offers a different angle: apologizing for companions' lapses, choosing hunger over gold, and declaring the world as the abode of the homeless. Together, they form a powerful lesson on spiritual priorities.

Guided Path
1
Read the three hadiths
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the Prophet's own words and the different contexts sink in.
Notice the chain of narrators and the explicit renunciation.
2
Identify the common theme
Look for the thread that ties all three hadiths together. What attitude is the Prophet consistently expressing?
Each hadith involves a rejection of worldly prosperity or status.
3
Analyze each context
Consider the specific situation of each hadith: the battle of Uhud, the offer of gold, and the general statement. How does the context shape the message?
The first hadith is about apologizing and disassociating, the second about choosing hunger, the third about the nature of the world.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: Why did the Prophet choose this path? What does it teach about our relationship with worldly possessions?
The Prophet's choice is a model, not a command for all. The lesson is about priorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي يوم أحد روى البخاري ( ۲۸۰٥ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً : « اللهم ؛ إنِّي أعتذرُ إليكَ ممَّا صنع هؤلاء ـ يعني : أصحابه ـ وأبرأُ إليكَ ممَّا صنع هؤلاء ـ يعني : المشركين ـ ». وقد روى الترمذي ( ٢٣٤٧ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي أمامة رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً : عرض عليَّ ربِّي ليجعل لي بطحاء مكَّةَ ذهباً ، قلتُ : يا ربِّ ؛ ولكن أشبع يوماً وأجوعُ يوماً ؛ فإذا جُعتُ تضرّعتُ إليكَ وذكرتُكَ ، وإذا شبعت شكرتُكَ وحمدتكَ ». وروى أحمد في ( المسند » ( ٧١/٦ ) من حديث السيدة عائشة رضي الله عنها مرفوعاً : « الدنيا دارُ مَنْ لا دارَ لهُ ، ومالُ مَنْ لا مالَ لهُ ، ولها يجمعُ مَنْ لا عقل له ».
And on the day of Uhud, al-Bukhari narrated (2805) from the hadith of our master Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: 'O Allah, I apologize to You for what these did – meaning his Companions – and I disassociate myself before You from what these did – meaning the polytheists.' And al-Tirmidhi narrated (2347) from the hadith of our master Abu Umamah, may Allah be pleased with him, raised: 'My Lord offered to make the plain of Mecca gold for me. I said: O Lord, but I will be satiated one day and hungry one day; when I am hungry I will supplicate to You and remember You, and when I am satiated I will thank You and praise You.' And Ahmad narrated in the Musnad (6/71) from the hadith of Lady Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, raised: 'The world is the abode of one who has no abode, and wealth of one who has no wealth, and for it gathers one who has no intellect.'
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage collects three prophetic hadiths that reinforce the theme of renouncing worldly attractions. The first hadith, from the day of Uhud, shows the Prophet apologizing to Allah for the actions of his Companions (who had disobeyed his order) and disassociating from the polytheists. The second hadith repeats the offer of gold for the plain of Mecca, with the Prophet choosing hunger and satiety alternately to maintain supplication and gratitude. The third hadith, from Aisha, strikingly reverses valuing Mecca's gold: the world is only for those who have no real home or wealth. Each hadith underscores that the Prophet intentionally avoided worldly accumulation as a model of spiritual virtue.

Key Terms
دنيا
أعتذر
أبرأ
تضرع
شكر
حمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These hadith might be misinterpreted as condemning all worldly possessions.
Correction: The Prophet's choice is voluntary asceticism, not a prohibition. The lesson is about priorities, not the inherent evil of worldly goods.

Checkpoint
What common theme do the three hadiths in this passage emphasize?
A) The importance of fighting polytheists.
B) The virtue of wealth and abundance.
C) The Prophet's renunciation of worldly pleasures.
D) The superiority of Mecca over other cities.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's renunciation models a life of spiritual dependence and gratitude, not the rejection of legitimate worldly needs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet chose hunger and satiety to maintain remembrance of Allah. If you were to introduce a similar rhythm into your life—deliberately inconveniencing yourself for the sake of drawing closer to Allah—what would that look like? What one tangible change can you make this week?
?
The Prophet said this world is for those with no real abode. Where is your true home? If you were to die tonight, would you feel prepared? What attachment to this world holds you back from that preparation, and how can you begin loosening its grip?
?
In the first hadith, the Prophet apologizes to Allah for his Companions' mistake and disassociates from the polytheists. Do you feel the same urgency to separate yourself from sin and disavow falsehood in your daily interactions? What is one specific situation where you are tolerating a compromise, and how can you make your allegiance to Allah more evident starting today?

Eschatological Terror and the Prophet's Intercession
Sanusi describes the angel of death, the fear of angels and prophets, and the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the vivid depiction of the Day of Judgment horrors and the unique intercession of Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession overpowers even the most terrifying moments of the Day.

Sanusi paints a terrifying scene of the angel of death, the helplessness of all creatures, and the moment when the Prophet Muhammad steps forward to intercede. This lesson explores that narrative and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the angel of death
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the sensory details: sound, darkness, fire.
2
Observe the reaction of angels and prophets
Notice that even the closest beings fall to their knees in fear. This emphasizes the magnitude of the situation.
3
Identify the Prophet's role
The Prophet rises toward the Fire, and the Fire hears a divine command. Recognize the supremacy of his intercession.
4
Reflect on the meaning
Consider what this scene tells us about the Prophet's rank and the mercy of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منكراً لا يُستطاع سماعه ، ويملأُ عليهم الجو ظلمة وناراً زيادةً على ما هم فيهِ مِنَ الأهوالِ الجسيمةِ ، ويلتقط الناسَ مِنَ الموقفِ ويبتلعُهم في ذلك العنق الطويل إلى جوفه !
وحينئذ تجثو الملائكة المقربون والأنبياء والرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام على الرُّكَبِ خوفاً مِنَ اللهِ تعالى ، فحينئذٍ ينهض إلى النارِ سيّد الخَلْقِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فتسمعُ النارُ حينئذ نداءً مِنْ قِبَلِ اللهِ تعالى : اسمعي له وأطيعي
وإِنَّما أطلتُ بعض الطولِ فيما يتعلَّقُ بنبوَّة نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ - وإنْ كانَ العلم بثبوتِ رسالتِهِ يكفي فيهِ أدنى مما ذكرتُ - لأنَّ حبَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ الذي كَمَنَ في القلب ، وقصد زيادة تحبيبه للناظرِ والمستمع ليحصل له بفضْلِ اللهِ تعالى كمال الإيمان ؛ حتى يجمع بين العلم والعمل . هو الذي حملني على ذلكَ ، ومَنْ أَحبَّ شيئاً أكثرَ مِنْ ذكرِهِ .
اللهمَّ ؛ إِنَّا نتوسل إليكَ بأكرم الخلْقِ عندَكَ ؛ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمدٍ صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ أن تجمع شملنا وشمل آبائنا وأمهاتنا وإخواننا وأحبتنا بنبيك سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في جنَّةِ الفردوس ، بلا محنةٍ ولا عقوبةٍ ولا معاتبة ، يا أرحم الراحمين .
A denier (i.e., the angel of death) whose sound cannot be endured, and he fills the air with darkness and fire, in addition to the immense terrors they are already in. He snatches people from the standing-place and swallows them into that long neck into his belly! At that moment, the cherubic angels, prophets, and messengers (peace and blessings be upon them) fall on their knees in fear of Allah the Exalted. Then the master of creation, our Prophet and our master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) rises towards the Fire. Then the Fire hears a call from Allah the Exalted: 'Listen to him and obey.' Indeed, I have prolonged somewhat regarding the prophethood of our Prophet, our master, and our liege-lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) — although knowledge of the establishment of his message would suffice with less than what I mentioned — because love for him (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), which resides in the heart, and the intention to increase love for him in the observer and listener so that he may attain, by the grace of Allah the Exalted, the perfection of faith — combining knowledge and action — that is what drove me to that. And whoever loves something mentions it frequently. O Allah, we beseech You through the noblest of creation to You, our master and our liege-lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), to gather our group and the group of our fathers, mothers, brothers, and loved ones with Your Prophet, our master and our liege-lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), in the Garden of Paradise, without trial, punishment, or reproach, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a vivid eschatological narrative describing the terrors of the Day of Judgment and the unique intercession of the Prophet Muhammad. It begins by depicting the angel of death (identified as a 'denier' in some interpretations) whose terrifying sound is unbearable, filling the atmosphere with darkness and fire, compounding the immense horrors already faced by people. The angel snatches people from the standing-place of judgment and swallows them into his long neck, a description emphasizing utter helplessness. Then even the closest angels, prophets, and messengers fall to their knees in fear of Allah. At this moment, the Prophet Muhammad, the master of creation, steps forward to intercede. The fire hears a divine command to listen to him and obey. The author explains that he has elaborated on the Prophet's prophethood not because it was necessary (since the proof of his message is sufficient with less) but out of love for him, aiming to increase love in the reader and listener, leading to perfect faith that combines knowledge and action. The passage concludes with a supplication beseeching Allah through the Prophet to gather all in Paradise without suffering.

Key Terms
منكر
الملائكة المقربون
الأنبياء والرسل
سيّد الخَلْق
النار
نداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'منكر' is a generic term for a denier, but in this context it refers specifically to the angel of death.
Correction: The word 'منكر' here is interpreted as the angel of death (Munkar) in this eschatological scene, not a generic denier.

Checkpoint
What happens when the Prophet Muhammad rises toward the Fire?
A) The Fire retreats
B) The Fire hears a command to listen and obey
C) The Fire extinguishes
D) The Fire attacks him

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's intercession is supreme, causing even the Fire to obey Allah's command through him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The cherubic angels and prophets fell to their knees in fear of Allah. Where is that fear in your life? Have you replaced awe with routine? What will you do today to rebuild that reverence?
?
Prophet Muhammad rose toward the Fire while everyone else was paralyzed by terror. Do you truly rely on his intercession as a living hope, or is it a distant fact? What step will you take this week to deepen your connection to him?
?
The Fire obeys a divine command through the Prophet. Your sins are part of the fuel of that Fire. How does this reality change the way you view your relationship with Allah and His Messenger? Will you let it move you to repentance now?

The Author's Loving Motive and Supplication
Sanusi explains his motive for elaboration and offers a supplication through the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi elaborated on the Prophet's prophethood and how he concludes with a heartfelt supplication.

Core Idea
Love for the Prophet drives both knowledge and action, leading to perfect faith.

After describing the Prophet's intercession, Sanusi explains that his detailed account stems from his love for the Prophet and his desire to instill that love in others. He then offers a moving supplication, beseeching Allah through the Prophet's rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of the author's motive
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the phrase 'love for him which resides in the heart'.
2
Understand the connection between love and perfect faith
Sanusi says that increasing love leads to perfect faith that combines knowledge and action. Reflect on this.
3
Read the supplication
Read the final prayer. Notice how it uses the Prophet as a means (tawassul) to ask for Paradise without suffering.
4
Reflect on the author's method
Consider why Sanusi included this personal note and supplication. How does it serve the reader's faith?

وحينئذ تجثو الملائكة المقربون والأنبياء والرُّسُل عليهم الصلاة والسلام على الرُّكَبِ خوفاً مِنَ اللهِ تعالى ، فحينئذٍ ينهض إلى النارِ سيّد الخَلْقِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فتسمعُ النارُ حينئذ نداءً مِنْ قِبَلِ اللهِ تعالى : اسمعي له وأطيعي
وإِنَّما أطلتُ بعض الطولِ فيما يتعلَّقُ بنبوَّة نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ - وإنْ كانَ العلم بثبوتِ رسالتِهِ يكفي فيهِ أدنى مما ذكرتُ - لأنَّ حبَّهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ الذي كَمَنَ في القلب ، وقصد زيادة تحبيبه للناظرِ والمستمع ليحصل له بفضْلِ اللهِ تعالى كمال الإيمان ؛ حتى يجمع بين العلم والعمل . هو الذي حملني على ذلكَ ، ومَنْ أَحبَّ شيئاً أكثرَ مِنْ ذكرِهِ .
اللهمَّ ؛ إِنَّا نتوسل إليكَ بأكرم الخلْقِ عندَكَ ؛ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمدٍ صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ أن تجمع شملنا وشمل آبائنا وأمهاتنا وإخواننا وأحبتنا بنبيك سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في جنَّةِ الفردوس ، بلا محنةٍ ولا عقوبةٍ ولا معاتبة ، يا أرحم الراحمين .
A denier (i.e., the angel of death) whose sound cannot be endured, and he fills the air with darkness and fire, in addition to the immense terrors they are already in. He snatches people from the standing-place and swallows them into that long neck into his belly! At that moment, the cherubic angels, prophets, and messengers (peace and blessings be upon them) fall on their knees in fear of Allah the Exalted. Then the master of creation, our Prophet and our master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) rises towards the Fire. Then the Fire hears a call from Allah the Exalted: 'Listen to him and obey.' Indeed, I have prolonged somewhat regarding the prophethood of our Prophet, our master, and our liege-lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) — although knowledge of the establishment of his message would suffice with less than what I mentioned — because love for him (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), which resides in the heart, and the intention to increase love for him in the observer and listener so that he may attain, by the grace of Allah the Exalted, the perfection of faith — combining knowledge and action — that is what drove me to that. And whoever loves something mentions it frequently. O Allah, we beseech You through the noblest of creation to You, our master and our liege-lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), to gather our group and the group of our fathers, mothers, brothers, and loved ones with Your Prophet, our master and our liege-lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), in the Garden of Paradise, without trial, punishment, or reproach, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a vivid eschatological narrative describing the terrors of the Day of Judgment and the unique intercession of the Prophet Muhammad. It begins by depicting the angel of death (identified as a 'denier' in some interpretations) whose terrifying sound is unbearable, filling the atmosphere with darkness and fire, compounding the immense horrors already faced by people. The angel snatches people from the standing-place of judgment and swallows them into his long neck, a description emphasizing utter helplessness. Then even the closest angels, prophets, and messengers fall to their knees in fear of Allah. At this moment, the Prophet Muhammad, the master of creation, steps forward to intercede. The fire hears a divine command to listen to him and obey. The author explains that he has elaborated on the Prophet's prophethood not because it was necessary (since the proof of his message is sufficient with less) but out of love for him, aiming to increase love in the reader and listener, leading to perfect faith that combines knowledge and action. The passage concludes with a supplication beseeching Allah through the Prophet to gather all in Paradise without suffering.

كمال الإيمان
العلم والعمل
التوسل

A) To prove it against deniers

D) To show off his knowledge

Love for the Prophet is essential for perfect faith, and we should often beseech Allah through him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi says love for the Prophet drove him to go beyond what was necessary. When was the last time your love for the Prophet drove you to do more than the minimum in your faith? Why does that love not burn as fiercely in your own heart?
?
Perfect faith combines knowledge and action. Right now, what is one area where you have knowledge about the Prophet's rights but lack corresponding action? What is one concrete step you will take today to close that gap?
?
Sanusi ends by beseeching Allah to be gathered with the Prophet without trial, punishment, or reproach. If you were to stand before Allah right now, would you be ready for that gathering? What are you doing each day to ensure you are among those whom the Prophet will intercede for?

Disagreement on the Best Prophet After Muhammad
Sanusi quotes Taftazani listing disagreements on who is best among prophets after Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different scholarly opinions on who is considered the best prophet after Muhammad (SAW) and the reasoning behind each opinion.

Core Idea
After Muhammad, the ranking of prophets is disputed—each opinion highlights a unique virtue.

This passage from Sanusi quotes at-Taftazani, who lists five opinions on which prophet is best after Muhammad. While all Muslims agree that Muhammad is the greatest, scholars have debated the relative merits of other major prophets. Each opinion is supported by a specific excellence, such as Adam's fatherhood or Moses' direct conversation with Allah. This lesson presents those views as recorded in the kalam tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the introductory structure and the list of opinions.
The passage begins with a 'First Reminder' and cites Taftazani.
2
Identify the five opinions
List each prophet mentioned and the reasoning given for their superiority over others after Muhammad.
3
Compare the reasons
Notice how each reason emphasizes a different aspect of prophethood: lineage, devotion, trust, special communication, or spiritual status.
4
Understand the context
This is a doctrinal discussion within the broader topic of the best of creation, but it does not affect the consensus on Muhammad's supremacy.
5
Reflect on the disagreement
Consider why such a disagreement exists and what it teaches about the diversity of scholarly opinion in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیهات الأول
في اختلافهم في الأفضل بعدَهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ]
قال التفتازاني في شرح المقاصدِ الدينيَّةِ » له بعد ما ذكرَ الإجماع على أنَّه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضلُ الأنبياء والرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام : ( اختلفوا في الأفضل بعده :
فقيل : آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لكونه أبا البشر وقيل : نوح عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ لطول عبادته ومجاهدته . وقيل : إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لزيادة توكَّلِهِ واطمئنانه وقيل : موسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ لكونه كليم الله تعالى ونجيه .
وقيل : عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ لكونه روح الله وصفيه )
First Reminder: Regarding their disagreement on the best after him (may Allah bless him and grant him peace). At-Taftazani said in his commentary 'Sharh al-Maqasid ad-Diniyya', after he mentioned the consensus that he (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) is the best of the prophets and messengers (peace and blessings be upon them): (They disagreed on the best after him: It was said: Adam (peace be upon him) because he is the father of humanity. And it was said: Noah (peace be upon him) due to the length of his worship and his struggle. And it was said: Abraham (peace be upon him) due to his greater trust and serenity. And it was said: Moses (peace be upon him) because he is the interlocutor of Allah the Exalted and His intimate. And it was said: Jesus (peace be upon him) because he is the spirit of Allah and His chosen one.)
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is a classification of opinions regarding the ranking of prophets after Muhammad (SAW). It is introduced as a 'first reminder' (تنبیهات الأول) about a theological disagreement. Sanusi quotes at-Taftazani from his work 'Sharh al-Maqasid ad-Diniyya', who notes that although there is consensus that Muhammad is the best of all prophets and messengers, scholars differed on who is the best among the other prophets after him. The passage then lists five opinions with their rationales: (1) Adam because he is the father of humanity; (2) Noah because of his long worship and struggle; (3) Abraham for his greater trust and serenity; (4) Moses because he spoke directly to Allah and was His intimate; (5) Jesus because he is the spirit of Allah and His chosen one. The list is not exhaustive but represents the main views. The passage does not resolve the disagreement but merely reports it. This reflects the classical kalam practice of documenting differing scholarly positions on non-essential matters.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The disagreement implies that some prophets are better than Muhammad, or that the consensus on Muhammad's superiority is uncertain.
Correction: The disagreement is only about the relative ranking of other prophets after Muhammad; all agree that Muhammad is the best.

Checkpoint

A) Because he is the father of humanity.
B) Due to the length of his worship and his struggle.
C) Because he spoke directly to Allah.

Key Takeaway
While the ranking of prophets after Muhammad is disputed, each opinion highlights a distinct virtue of the prophet in question.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the virtues highlighted for each prophet—like Noah's long worship or Abraham's trust—which one challenges you most about your own spiritual life? What one step can you take this week to embody that virtue more deeply?
?

?
These opinions were offered by scholars who loved all prophets. Is there a prophet you feel personally distant from? How can you use the virtue mentioned in this lesson as a bridge to draw closer to him and to Allah?

The Unseen Matters and the Book's Purpose
Sanusi lists the unseen matters that must be believed and states the purpose of his book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key unseen matters that must be believed according to Sunni creed and the purpose of Sanusi's treatise in freeing the believer from blind imitation.

Core Idea
Belief in the unseen afterlife details is essential, but this book focuses on freeing you from blind imitation.

Sanusi concludes his creedal summary by listing the unseen matters reported by the Sharia. These include resurrection, grave questioning, the Sirat, Mizan, Hawd, and intercession. He then clarifies that the purpose of his brief treatise is not to provide exhaustive details but to equip the believer with core creedal knowledge to leave blind imitation behind.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the list of unseen matters and the statement of purpose at the end.
Pay attention to the phrase 'al-‘ujala' (brief treatise) and what it aims to achieve.
2
Identify the unseen matters listed
From the passage, extract the specific items of the unseen that Sanusi mentions. They are: resurrection of the same body, grave questioning, Sirat, Mizan, Hawd, intercession, and eternal bliss/punishment.
These are all matters of the sam'iyyat (audible matters) reported by revelation.
3
Understand the purpose of the treatise
Sanusi states that the intention of this brief work is only to free the legally responsible person from blind imitation (taqlid) in creed. Detailed knowledge of these matters is found in fiqh and hadith books.
This clarifies that the book is a concise creedal primer, not an exhaustive manual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالمغيبات التي أخبر عنها الشرع فوجب تصديقه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في كلِّ ما أتى بهِ عَنِ اللَّهِ تعالى ؛ كالبعث لعين هذا البدنِ لا لمثلِهِ إجماعاً ، ونحوِهِ مِنْ سؤال القبر ونعيمِهِ وعذابِهِ ، والصراط ، والميزان ، والحوض، والشفاعة للعصاةِ المؤمنينَ في إنقاذهم مِنَ النارِ بعد نفوذ الوعيدِ في جماعة منهم إجماعاً، وتأبيد نعيم المؤمنين وعذاب الكافرين . ومعرفة تفاصيل ما أتى بهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مُبيَّنٌ في كُتُبِ الأئمةِ مِنَ الفقه والحديثِ ، والقَصْدُ بهذهِ العُجالةِ إِنَّما هو ذكرُ ما يَخرجُ بهِ المكلَّفُ عن التقليد في العقائدِ ، وفَهْمُ هذهِ الجُمَلِ وافٍ بذلكَ إِنْ يَسَّرَ الله سبحانَهُ أَتمَّ وفاء وهو جلَّ وعلا المستعانُ والمسؤولُ أنْ يخرجنا بفضلِهِ ويُخرِجَ بنا مِنَ الظلماتِ إلى النورِ ، وأنْ يكرمنا ويكرم على أيدينا بما يُوجِبُ لنا ولأحبَّتِنا مِنَ التنعم في أعلى الفردوس بشريف معرفتِهِ ولذيذ رؤيتِهِ أعظم سرورٍ ، وصلَّى اللهُ على سيدنا محمد عدد ما ذكره الذاكرونَ ، وغفل عن ذكرِهِ الغافلونَ ، ورضي الله تعالى عن أصحاب رسولِ اللهِ صلَّى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ أجمعين ، والحمد الله ربِّ العالمين.
Belief in the unseen matters that the Sharia has informed of. So it is obligatory to believe him (the Prophet), may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in everything he brought from Allah Almighty; such as the resurrection of this very body not its like by consensus, and similar matters from the questioning of the grave and its bliss and its punishment, and the Path (Sirat), and the Balance (Mizan), and the Basin (Hawd), and intercession for sinful believers to rescue them from the Fire after the threat has been fulfilled for a group of them by consensus, and the eternal bliss of believers and punishment of disbelievers. And the knowledge of the details of what he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, brought is explained in the books of the imams of fiqh and hadith. The intention of this brief treatise is only to mention that by which the legally responsible person exits from blind imitation in creeds. Understanding these summaries is sufficient for that, if Allah glorified makes it fully sufficient. He, exalted and majestic, is the Helper and the One asked to bring us out by His grace and to bring others out by us from darkness to light, and to honor us and honor through us that which necessitates for us and for our loved ones the delight in the highest Paradise through the noble knowledge of Him and the delicious vision of Him, the greatest joy. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad as many times as those who remember Him have remembered, and as many times as those who are heedless of His remembrance have been heedless, and may Allah be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a concluding summary of the obligatory beliefs concerning the unseen (al-mughayyabat) and a statement of the book's purpose. The author first asserts that belief in the unseen matters reported by the Sharia is required. He then lists several key eschatological items: the bodily resurrection (ba'th) of the very same body ('ayn hadha al-badan) not a likeness, the grave's questioning and its reward/punishment, the Sirat (bridge), the Mizan (scales), the Hawd (basin), and intercession (shafa'a) for sinful believers – with the note that some believers will still enter the Fire but then be rescued by intercession. He also mentions the eternal nature of paradise for believers and hell for disbelievers. He notes that detailed knowledge of these matters is found in fiqh and hadith books. Then he clarifies the purpose of this brief treatise (al-'ujala): it is to provide the core creedal points that free the mukallaf (legally responsible person) from blind imitation (taqlid) in beliefs. Understanding these summaries (jumal) is sufficient for that goal. The passage ends with a prayer for divine help, honor, and the ultimate joy of knowledge and vision of Allah, followed by salutations on the Prophet and his Companions, and praise to Allah.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This book is meant to provide all details of religious practice and afterlife matters.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that detailed knowledge is found in fiqh and hadith books; his treatise only aims to free the mukallaf from blind imitation in creed.

D) To list all the hadiths about the grave.

Key Takeaway
The core unseen matters of the Hereafter are resurrection, grave questioning, Sirat, Mizan, Hawd, and intercession, and this book aims to free the believer from blind imitation in creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would change if you lived with absolute certainty that these events are imminent?

Resurrection of Bodies: Consensus and the Correct Position of Tawaqquf
Sanusi affirms the consensus on bodily resurrection and explains the correct stance of tawaqquf on modality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the resurrection of bodies is definitively established by consensus, and that the correct theological position regarding its modality is suspension of judgment (tawaqquf).

Core Idea
Resurrection is certain; its 'how' is wisely left open.

Sanusi opens a discussion on the resurrection of bodies by affirming its absolute certainty based on the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus of all religions. He then notes a subtle disagreement among Ahl al-Sunnah about the precise modality—whether God creates the body anew from nothing or reassembles it from dispersed parts. The lesson explains why the safest, most precise position is to suspend judgment on the modality while firmly affirming the resurrection of the very same body.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse every detail. Then read the translation to get an overall sense of the author's argument.
Notice that Sanusi moves from certainty to disagreement to a resolution.
2
Identify the two levels of discussion
First, Sanusi presents the fact of resurrection as definitive. Second, he introduces a difference about its modality. Separate these two in your mind.
3
Understand the principle of tawaqquf
Ask yourself: why does Sanusi say the truth is tawaqquf? The commentary explains that both modalities are intellectually possible and no decisive scripture specifies which occurs.
This is a key method in kalam: when reason permits multiple options and revelation is silent, one suspends judgment.
4
Note the author's creedal formulation
Sanusi explains why he phrased his creed as 'resurrection of this very body, not a like body' — to affirm the certainty of the identity while leaving the modality open.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على حشر الأجساد وهو فمِنَ المقطوع بهِ الذي جاءَ كتاباً وسنة وإجماعاً : إعادة الخلْقِ بأعيانهم بعد إهلاكهم : وقد أجمعَتِ الشرائعُ كلّها على ذلكَ ، مِنَ المعلومِ مِنَ الدينِ ضرورةً ، فلا حاجة إلى التطويل بسرد الأدلَّةِ العقلية والنقليَّةِ في ذلك ثم وقع الاختلافُ بينَ أهل السنَّةِ : هل تلك الإعادة بالإيجاد بعد العدم المحض ، أو بالجمع بعد تفريق الأجزاء ؟ والحقُّ : التوقف في ذلكَ ، وهو اختيار إمام الحرمين ؛ إذْ كلٌّ مِنَ الأمرين جائز عقلاً في قدرةِ المولى جلَّ وعزّ ، ولم يرد قاطع مِنَ الشرع بتعيين الواقع منهما(١) ، فكانَ الأحوطُ الوقفَ ، والله تعالى أعلم ، ولهذا اقتصرتُ في أصلِ العقيدةِ على قولي : ( كالبعث لعين هذا البدنِ لا لمثلِهِ إجماعاً ( يعني : أنَّ المحقق في البعث بالإجماع أنَّ عينَ هذا البدن الذي كان في الدنيا يطيع ويعصي . . هو الذي يُبعَثُ ، لا أَنَّ
The discourse on the resurrection of bodies. And it is among the definitively established matters which came in Book, Sunnah, and consensus: the return of the creation in their very selves after their destruction. And all the religions have agreed upon that; it is known from the religion by necessity, so there is no need to lengthen by enumerating intellectual and transmitted proofs regarding that. Then a difference occurred among Ahl al-Sunnah: Is that return by creation after absolute non-existence, or by gathering after the dispersal of parts? And the truth is suspension of judgment regarding that, and it is the choice of Imam al-Haramayn; since each of the two matters is intellectually possible within the power of the Lord, Glorious and Exalted, and no decisive proof has come from the Sharia specifying which of them actually occurred, so the most cautious was suspension. And Allah Almighty knows best. And for this reason I confined myself in the original creed to my statement: 'like the resurrection of this very body, not its likeness, by consensus,' meaning that what is established in resurrection by consensus is that this very body which was in the world, obeying and disobeying, is what is resurrected, not that...
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage focuses specifically on the resurrection of bodies. The author first states that it is definitively established by the three primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, consensus) that the creation will be returned in their very selves after destruction. He notes that all religions agree, making it known by necessity, so lengthy proofs are unnecessary. Then he highlights a difference among Ahl al-Sunnah: is the resurrection a creation after absolute non-existence (i.e., creating anew) or a gathering after dispersal of parts (i.e., reassembling the same body)? He declares the true position is tawaqquf (suspension of judgment), following Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, because both are intellectually possible for God's power, and no decisive scriptural proof specifies which one actually occurs. Hence tawaqquf is the cautious approach. Finally, he explains why he phrased his creed as 'like the resurrection of this very body, not its likeness, by consensus': to emphasize that the actual body that existed in the world is resurrected, not a similar body. This is the agreed-upon point.

Key Terms

إعادة الخلق بأعيانهم
الإيجاد بعد العدم المحض
الجمع بعد تفريق الأجزاء
التوقف
إمام الحرمين
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the difference among Ahl al-Sunnah questions the fact of resurrection itself.
Correction: The passage clearly states that the resurrection of the same body is a matter of consensus. The disagreement is only about the modality—how God brings it about—not about whether it happens.

Checkpoint
On what point do Ahl al-Sunnah disagree regarding resurrection?
A) Whether resurrection occurs at all
B) Whether it is creation after non-existence or gathering after dispersal
C) Whether the body is the same or different
D) Whether it is known by reason or revelation

Key Takeaway
The resurrection of the same body is certain; the exact mode of its re-creation is unknown and thus we suspend judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe with certainty that this very body will be raised. Yet, you may live as if that day will never come. What is one sin you continue in because you forget that the body you use to commit it is the same body that will stand before Allah? Commit today to abandoning that sin, seeking Allah's forgiveness.
?
The lesson teaches us to suspend judgment on the modality of resurrection, trusting Allah's wisdom. Is there an aspect of your faith that you have insisted on understanding fully before submitting? Name it, and practice saying 'I believe, and I entrust the knowledge to Allah.'

The Reality of Punishment and Pleasure in the Grave
Sanusi affirms the reality of grave punishment and pleasure, citing consensus and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus on the reality of grave punishment and pleasure, the rejection of objections, and the scriptural proofs from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The grave is a real place of reward and punishment, not just a hole in the ground.

Sanusi begins by affirming the reality of punishment and pleasure in the grave, stating that this is a matter of consensus among Muslims. He then addresses a misconception attributing denial to the Mu'tazila, clarifying that it was only a small group. Finally, he presents the Quranic verses and hadiths that establish this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus
Read the first part where Sanusi states that Muslims unanimously agree on the questioning, punishment, and pleasure in the grave. Note that disagreement is attributed to some Mu'tazila and later scholars.
The consensus is a strong foundation for the doctrine.
2
Examine the refutation
Look at the quote from Sharh al-Maqasid that denial is only reported from Dirar ibn Amr, and that the Mu'tazila are innocent of this view. Understand that this protects the orthodox position.
Dirar ibn Amr was a known deviant figure.
3
Study the Quranic proofs
Review each verse cited: the family of Pharaoh exposed to fire morning and evening (before Resurrection); Noah's people drowned then admitted to fire; two deaths and two lives; martyrs alive and provided for. See how each indicates an intermediate state after death.
These verses are interpreted as referring to the grave (barzakh).
4
Study the hadith proofs
Read the hadiths: the grave is a garden or pit from Hell; the Prophet passing by two graves being punished; the two angels with hammers questioning the deceased. Note the multiplicity of such reports.
These hadiths are mutawatir in meaning, providing certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على عذاب القبر ونعيمه وأمَّا سؤال القبرِ ، وعذابُهُ للكفَّارِ ولبعض عصاة المؤمنينَ ، ونعيمه : فقد أجمعَ الإسلاميُّونَ على أنَّ ذلكَ حقٌّ واقع لا ريبَ فِيهِ ، ونُسب خلافُ ذلك إلى بعض المعتزلة وبعض المتأخّرينَ . قال : ( إِنَّما حُكِيَ إنكار ذلكَ عن ضرارِ بنِ عمرو ، وإِنَّما نُسِبَ إلى المعتزلة وهم برآءُ منهُ ؛ لمخالطة ضرارِ إِيَّاهم ، وتبعَهُ قومٌ مِنَ السفهاء المعاندين للحق ) ودليلُ أهل الحقِّ : كقولِهِ تعالى في آلِ فرعونَ : ﴿ النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوا وَعَشِيَّا ﴾ [غافر : ٤٦] أي : قبل القيامة ، وذلك في القبرِ ؛ بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ أَدْخِلُوا ءَالَ فِرْعَوْنَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَابِ ﴾ [غافر : ٤٦] وكقوله تعالى في قومِ نوح : ﴿ أُغْرِقُوا فَأُدْخِلُوا نَارًا ﴾ [نوح : ٢٥] ، والفاء للتعقيب وكقوله تعالى : ﴿ رَبَّنَا أَمَتَّنَا اثْنَتَيْنِ وَأَحْيَيْتَنَا اثْنَتَيْنِ ﴾ [غافر : ١١] ، وإحدى الحياتين ليست إلا في القبر وكقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتًا بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ * فَرِحِينَ بِمَا ءَاتَنُهُمُ اللَّهُ مِن فَضْلِهِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٦٩-١٧٠] . والأحاديث المتواترة المعنى : كقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام القَبْرُ رَوْضَةٌ مِنْ رِيَاضِ الْجَنَّةِ ، أَوْ حُفْرَةٌ مِنْ حُفَرِ النِّيرَانِ . ولما رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ مرَّ بقبرين فقالَ : « إِنَّهُمَا يُعَذِّبَانِ ، وَمَا يُعَذِّبَانِ فِي كَبِيرٍ ... » الحديث . وكالحديثِ المشهور في الملكينِ اللَّذين يدخلان القبر ومعهما مِرْزَبَتَانِ ، فيسألان الميت عن ربَّهِ ، وعن دينه ، وعن نبيه ، إلى ذلك غيرِ مِنَ الأخبار والآثارِ المسطورة في الكتب المشهورة ، وقد تواتر عنِ النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ استعاذتُهُ مِنْ عذابِ القبرِ واستفاضَ ذلكَ في الأدعية المأثورة .
Discussion on the punishment of the grave and its pleasure. As for the questioning of the grave, its punishment for the disbelievers and for some sinful believers, and its pleasure: the Muslims have unanimously agreed that that is true and real, no doubt about it. And disagreement with that is attributed to some of the Mu'tazila and some of the later scholars. He said: 'Denial of that is only reported from Dirar ibn Amr, and it was only attributed to the Mu'tazila while they are innocent of it, due to Dirar mixing with them, and a people of foolish ones who stubbornly oppose the truth followed him.' And the proof of the people of truth: like His statement, exalted, concerning the family of Pharaoh: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening' [Ghafir: 46] i.e., before the Resurrection, and that is in the grave; as evidence of His statement, exalted: 'And on the Day the Hour comes, admit the family of Pharaoh to the severest punishment' [Ghafir: 46]. And like His statement, exalted, concerning the people of Noah: 'They were drowned and then admitted to a Fire' [Nuh: 25], and the 'fa' indicates sequence. And like His statement, exalted: 'Our Lord, You made us die two deaths and made us live two lives' [Ghafir: 11], and one of the two lives is only in the grave. And like His statement, exalted: 'And do not think those who are killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision, rejoicing in what Allah has given them of His bounty' [Aal-Imran: 169-170]. And the hadiths of recurrent meaning: like his saying, peace be upon him: 'The grave is a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' And according to what was narrated that he, peace be upon him, passed by two graves and said: 'Indeed, they are being punished, and they are not being punished for something great...' the hadith. And like the famous hadith about the two angels who enter the grave with two iron hammers, and they ask the deceased about his Lord, his religion, and his prophet, and other such reports and traditions recorded in famous books, and it has been recurrently narrated from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he sought refuge from the punishment of the grave, and that spread widely in the supplications transmitted.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is an affirmation and proof of the reality of the punishment and pleasure in the grave ('adhab al-qabr wa na'eemuhu). The author begins by stating the consensus (ijma') of the Muslims that the questioning in the grave, punishment for disbelievers and some sinful believers, and pleasure are true and real without doubt. He then notes that disagreement is attributed to some Mu'tazila and later scholars, but quotes a rebuttal from al-Sa'd in Sharh al-Maqasid that the denial is only reported from Dirar ibn Amr, and the Mu'tazila are innocent of it; rather, foolish opponents followed Dirar. This defends the orthodox position. The author then provides scriptural proofs from the Qur'an and hadith. The first verse: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening' (Ghafir 40:46) is interpreted as referring to before the Resurrection, i.e., in the grave, because the next verse says on the Day of Resurrection they will be admitted to severer punishment. Second: the verse about Noah's people being drowned and then admitted to fire (Nuh 71:25), with the letter 'fa' indicating immediate sequence, implying punishment after drowning before the Resurrection, which is in the grave. Third: the verse 'Our Lord, You made us die two deaths and made us live two lives' (Ghafir 40:11), where one of the two lives is understood to be in the grave (the intermediate life, barzakh). Fourth: the verse about martyrs being alive and receiving provision (Aal-Imran 3:169-170) indicates life after death before the Resurrection. Then the author cites hadiths of recurrent meaning (mutawatir ma'nawiyan): the grave is a garden or a pit from Hell; the Prophet passing by two graves and saying they are being punished; and the hadith of the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) who question the deceased. He concludes that such reports are numerous and the Prophet's seeking refuge from punishment of the grave is widely transmitted. This collectively establishes the doctrine.

المعتزلة
أهل الحق
الآيات
الأحاديث المتواترة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazila as a school deny punishment in the grave.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that only Dirar ibn Amr held this view; the Mu'tazila are innocent of it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group is initially wrongly accused of denying punishment in the grave?
A) The Khawarij
B) The Mu'tazila
C) The Ash'aris
D) The Jahmiyyah

Key Takeaway
Punishment and pleasure in the grave are real, established by consensus, Quranic verses, and mutawatir hadith, and rejection is attributed only to a tiny fringe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live with the awareness that your grave is being prepared right now—either as a garden from Paradise or a pit from Hellfire? What would change in your daily life if you really believed the next moment after death could bring immediate reward or punishment?
?
The Prophet ﷺ regularly sought refuge from the punishment of the grave in his supplications. How often do you sincerely make this duʿā', and what does your lack of it reveal about the depth of your faith in this reality?
?
If the angels were to enter your grave tonight and ask you about your Lord, your religion, and your prophet, could you answer with certainty and confidence? What practical steps are you taking today to prepare for that unavoidable interrogation?

Proofs for Punishment of the Grave
Sanusi cites Quran and hadith to prove punishment of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic and hadith evidence for the punishment of the grave and why it is considered an established doctrine in Sunni Islam.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is proven by the Quran, mutawatir hadith, and the Prophet's own supplication.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the scriptural foundations for the reality of punishment in the grave. He cites two Quranic verses that hint at an intermediate state of life, then invokes multiple hadiths that describe the grave as either a garden or a pit, the interrogation by angels, and the Prophet's own seeking refuge from this punishment. These evidences form part of the samiyyat—matters known only through revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
Find the two verses from Ghafir and Al Imran. Understand how they imply life or punishment in the grave.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Look at the mutawatir-in-meaning hadiths: grave as garden or pit, two graves being punished, the two angels with hammers.
The author emphasizes that these hadiths are mutawatir in meaning, not necessarily in exact wording.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's practice
Notice that the Prophet himself sought refuge from punishment of the grave, which reinforces the doctrine.
This is an additional supporting evidence.
5
Summarize the overall argument
Combine the Quran and hadith evidence to form the complete basis for the belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكقوله تعالى : ﴿ رَبَّنَا أَمَتَنَا اثْنَيْنِ وَأَحْيَيْتَنَا اثْنَتَيْنِ [غافر : ١١] ، وإحدى الحياتين ليست إلا في القبر وكقوله تعالى : ( وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتًا بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ * فَرِحِينَ بِمَا ءَاتَنْهُمُ اللَّهُ مِن فَضْلِهِ ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٦٩-١٧٠] . والأحاديث المتواترة المعنى : كقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام القَبْرُ رَوْضَةٌ مِنْ رِيَاضِ الْجَنَّةِ ، أَوْ حُفْرَةٌ مِنْ حُفَرِ النِّيرَانِ. ولما رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ مرَّ بقبرين فقالَ : « إِنَّهُمَا يُعَذِّبَانِ ، وَمَا يُعَذِّبَانِ فِي كَبِيرٍ ... » الحديث. وكالحديثِ المشهور في الملكينِ اللَّذين يدخلان القبر ومعهما مِرْزَبَتَانِ ، فيسألان الميت عن ربَّهِ ، وعن دينه ، وعن نبيه ، إلى ذلك غيرِ مِنَ الأخبار والآثارِ المسطورة في الكتب المشهورة ، وقد تواتر عنِ النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ استعاذتُهُ مِنْ عذابِ القبرِ واستفاضَ ذلكَ في الأدعية المأثورة. نسأله سبحانَهُ أنْ يعاملنا في الدنيا والآخرة بمخض فضله وكرمه ، ولا يؤاخذنا بأعمالنا الخبيثة ، إنه ذو الفضل العظيم
And like His statement, the Most High: 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice' [Ghafir: 11], and one of the two lives is only in the grave. And like His statement, the Most High: 'And do not think those who have been killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision, rejoicing in what Allah has given them of His bounty' [Al 'Imran: 169-170]. And the hadiths that are mutawatir in meaning: like his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'The grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' And because it was narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, passed by two graves and said: 'Indeed, they are being punished, and they are not being punished for something great...' the hadith. And like the well-known hadith about the two angels who enter the grave with two iron hammers, and they ask the deceased about his Lord, his religion, and his prophet, and other such reports and narrations recorded in famous books. And it has been transmitted by tawatur from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, his seeking refuge from the punishment of the grave, and this is widespread in the transmitted supplications. We ask Him, glorified be He, to treat us in this world and the Hereafter with pure grace and generosity, and not to take us to task for our evil deeds; indeed, He is the Possessor of great bounty.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the reality of punishment of the grave (عذاب القبر). The author cites two Quranic verses: first, from Surah Ghafir (40:11) where the disbelievers say they were given two deaths and two lives—one of those lives is interpreted as life in the grave, which implies there is some experience there. Second, from Surah Al 'Imran (3:169-170) about martyrs being alive with their Lord, which also points to a post-mortem state before the resurrection. Then he mentions hadiths that are mutawatir in meaning, meaning the number of narrators is so high that it is impossible they agreed on a lie, even if the exact wording varies. These include: the Prophet saying the grave is either a garden or a pit of Hell; the incident where he passed by two graves and said they are being punished for seemingly trivial matters; and the famous hadith of the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) who interrogate the deceased. The author concludes that the Prophet's own seeking refuge from punishment of the grave is well-known and transmitted repeatedly, confirming the doctrine. The passage ends with a prayer asking Allah for grace and forgiveness, showing the practical import of this belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
You will be asked by Munkar and Nakir about your Lord, your religion, and your prophet. If you were questioned right now, would you answer with certainty? What have you neglected that you need to address before that meeting?

Definition and Nature of al-Sirat (the Bridge)
Sanusi defines al-Sirat and presents scholarly disagreement on its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what al-Sirat is according to Ahl al-Sunnah and the scholarly disagreement about its nature as a simple surface or a bridge.

Core Idea
Al-Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, thinner than hair and sharper than a sword.

In this lesson, Sanusi introduces al-Sirat, the bridge that every soul must cross to enter Paradise. He affirms its reality based on authentic hadith and consensus, then presents the first of two scholarly views on its nature. Focus on the definition and the first opinion.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Start by reading the opening lines describing al-Sirat as a bridge stretched over Hell, which everyone must cross. Note the key phrases: 'thinner than a hair' and 'sharper than a sword'.
These descriptions are taken from authentic hadith.
2
Understand the consensus
The passage states that Ahl al-Sunnah agree on this description. This is important because it establishes the reality of al-Sirat as a physical object, not merely a metaphor.
3
Examine the first opinion
Ibn Dihaq reports that a group of scholars, including Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni, held that al-Sirat is 'simple' (basit) — a broad surface where all people stand and are held accountable. Read how they interpret the Prophet's description.
The second opinion (that it is a narrow bridge) is introduced but not completed on this page.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الصِّراطُ : فهو جسر ممدود على متنِ جَهَنَّمَ يَرِدُهُ الأَوَّلُونَ والآخرونَ ، لا طريق للجنَّةِ إلا عليه ؛ وهو أدقُ مِنَ الشعرِ وأَحدٌ مِنَ السيفِ ، على ما ورد به الحديث الصحيحُ ، وأجمعَ عليهِ أهلُ السنَّةِ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم قالَ ابنُ دهاق : ( ثم اختلفوا في صفتِهِ : فذهبَتْ فِرقةُ إلى أنَّهُ بسيطٌ ، يقفُ الناسُ بأجمعهم عليه ، وعليهِ ، يكون حسابهم ، وهذا ما ذهب إليه أبو الحسن رحمه الله تعالى(٢) وهو ما ذكره أبو المعالي آنفاً حيثُ قالَ : ( يَردُهُ الأولون والآخرون ، فإذا توافوا عليه قيلَ للملائكةِ : قفوهم إنَّهم مسؤولون ، وجعلوا وصفه عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ لهُ بالدقةِ كالشعر والحد كالسيف وأكثر . . في بساطته ومِنْ أهل العلم - وهم الأكثرونَ - مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّ الصراط جسر طرفه
As for al-Sirat (the Bridge): it is a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, which the first and the last will come to; there is no path to Paradise except over it. It is thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, according to what the authentic hadith has reported, and the people of the Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them, are in agreement on it. Ibn Dihaq said: 'Then they differed regarding its nature. A group held that it is simple (basit); all people stand upon it, and upon it is their accounting. This is what Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, held, and it is what Abu al-Ma'ali mentioned earlier when he said: 'The first and the last will come to it; when they gather upon it, it is said to the angels: Stop them; indeed, they will be questioned.' And they made his description, peace and blessings be upon him, of it as delicate as hair and sharp as a sword and more... in its simplicity. And among the people of knowledge—and they are the majority—some said that al-Sirat is a bridge, its end...'
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage defines al-Sirat (the Bridge) and presents a scholarly disagreement about its nature. The author states that al-Sirat is a literal bridge stretched over Hell, which everyone must cross to enter Paradise. It is described as thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, based on authentic hadith, and this is agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah. The author then cites Ibn Dihaq, who records that scholars disagreed about its nature: one group (including Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni) held that it is 'simple' (بسيط), meaning a broad surface upon which all people stand and are held accountable. They interpret the Prophet's descriptions of its thinness and sharpness as referring to its simplicity or perhaps its difficulty for the wicked. The other opinion, attributed to the majority, is that it is a bridge (جسر) with a starting point and endpoint—likely implying a narrow path that people cross, with the righteous passing quickly and the sinful falling off. The commentary follows the author's order: first the definition and consensus, then the disagreement and the first opinion, and notes that the second opinion is introduced but not completed on this page.

Key Terms

الجسر
بسيط
أدق من الشعر
أحد من السيف
متن جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Sirat is only a metaphorical or spiritual crossing, not a real physical bridge.
Correction: The passage affirms that al-Sirat is a real bridge stretched over Hell, as reported in authentic hadith and agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the characteristic of al-Sirat that is agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah?
A) It is a simple surface
B) It is a bridge with two ends
C) It is thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword
D) It is only for the first generations

Key Takeaway
Al-Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, unanimously described as thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, with a scholarly debate about whether it is a wide surface or a narrow bridge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You will stand on a bridge thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword. Are you preparing your footing today, or are you walking carelessly toward an edge you cannot see? What specific sin do you need to abandon now to lighten your steps on that day?
?
The scholars disagreed on whether the Bridge is wide or narrow, but none doubted it is real. Do you live as if crossing al-Sirat is a certainty for you? If you truly believed your next step could land on that Bridge, what would you change about how you speak, how you treat others, or how you pray tonight?
?
Al-Sirat is the only path to Paradise; there is no other route. What if your deeds are so thin they cannot hold you? What act of obedience have you been delaying that could become your lifeline across the fire? Commit to doing it before the sun sets one more time.

The Sirat: Definition and the First Opinion
Defines the Sirat and presents the first opinion on its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Sirat as a real physical bridge over Hell and the first scholarly opinion that it is a simple surface upon which all people stand for reckoning.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge sharper than a sword, finer than hair — and the first view says it’s all one surface.

Sanusi begins his discussion of the Sirat by defining it as a physical bridge over Hell that every person must cross. He then presents the first of two opinions about its nature, attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who held that the Sirat is 'simple' — a single surface where all humanity gathers for judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the concrete description of the Sirat. Note that it is based on hadith and consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah.
The description 'finer than a hair, sharper than a sword' emphasizes its narrowness and peril.
2
Identify the first opinion
After the definition, Ibn Dahaq reports a difference. The first opinion says the Sirat is 'simple' (basit), meaning all people stand on it together for reckoning.
This view is attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and mentioned by Abu al-Ma'ali.
3
Connect to the larger discussion
Recognize that this is the first of two opinions; the second will follow in the next lesson. The difference is about the shape of the Sirat.
