وأمَّا الصِّراطُ : فهو جسر ممدود على متنِ جَهَنَّمَ يَرِدُهُ الأَوَّلُونَ والآخرونَ ، لا طريق للجنَّةِ إلا عليه ؛ وهو أدقُ مِنَ الشعرِ وأَحدٌ مِنَ السيفِ ، على ما ورد به الحديث الصحيحُ ، وأجمعَ عليهِ أهلُ السنَّةِ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم. قالَ ابنُ دهاق : ( ثم اختلفوا في صفتِهِ : فذهبَتْ فِرقةُ إلى أنَّهُ بسيطٌ ، يقفُ الناسُ بأجمعهم عليه ، وعليهِ ، يكون حسابهم ، وهذا ما ذهب إليه أبو الحسن رحمه الله تعالى وهو ما ذكره أبو المعالي آنفاً حيثُ قالَ : ( يَردُهُ الأولون والآخرون ، فإذا توافوا عليه قيلَ للملائكةِ : قفوهم إنَّهم مسؤولون ، وجعلوا وصفه عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ لهُ بالدقةِ كالشعر والحد كالسيف وأكثر . . في بساطته ).
As for the Sirat: it is a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, which the first and last will arrive at; there is no path to Paradise except over it; and it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, according to what is reported in the authentic hadith, and the Ahl al-Sunnah, may Allah be pleased with them, have agreed upon it. Ibn Dahaq said: (Then they differed concerning its description: one group went that it is simple, that all people stand on it together, and on it their reckoning takes place, and this is what Abu al-Hasan, may Allah have mercy on him, held, and it is what Abu al-Ma'ali mentioned earlier when he said: 'The first and last will arrive at it; then when they have assembled upon it, it will be said to the angels: Stop them, for they are to be questioned,' and they made his description, peace and blessings be upon him, of its fineness like hair and sharpness like a sword and more... upon its simplicity.)
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage defines the Sirat (the bridge over Hell) and presents the first of two opinions about its nature. The definition establishes that the Sirat is a real, physical bridge stretched over the surface of Hell. All people, from the first to the last, will come to it, and no one can enter Paradise except by crossing it. Its description—finer than a hair and sharper than a sword—comes from an authentic hadith and is agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah. Then Ibn Dahaq reports a difference of opinion about its description. The first opinion, attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and mentioned by Abu al-Ma'ali, holds that the Sirat is 'simple' (بسيط), meaning it is a single surface upon which all people stand, and on it they are judged. This view interprets the hadith's description of fineness and sharpness as referring to its extreme narrowness and peril, emphasizing the difficulty of crossing.

حديث
أهل السنة

Correction: The passage affirms it as a real physical bridge over Hell, based on authentic hadith and consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

?

The Nature of the Sirat: A Physical Bridge According to the Majority
Majority opinion on the Sirat as a physical bridge over the Fire with two ends.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority opinion on the Sirat as a physical bridge spanning from the earth of resurrection to Paradise, and the role of the Fire in the afterlife journey.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real, physical bridge—one end in the gathering place, the other in Paradise, over Hellfire.

In this lesson, we explore the second opinion on the Sirat, held by the majority of scholars. They describe it as a tangible bridge that all souls must cross to reach Paradise. The passage also offers a vivid description of the Fire and its interaction with the arrogant, supported by a hadith and a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the description of the bridge and the Fire.
The passage includes a hadith and a Quranic verse that support the description.
2
Identify key features of the Sirat
Note where the two ends of the Sirat are located, what it spans over, and how the Fire is described.
The Fire emits 'necks' that drag the arrogant tyrants.
3
Connect the hadith and verse to the description
Consider how the hadith about the Fire knowing the arrogant and the verse 'There is none of you but will come to it' reinforce the majority view.
The verse is interpreted as referring to the Sirat crossing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومِنْ أهل العلم - وهم الأكثرونَ - مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّ الصراط جسر طرفه في أرض القيامةِ ، وطرفُهُ الثاني في أرض الجنَّةِ ، وعلى متن النارِ ، وقالوا : إنَّ أرضَ القيامةِ تكونُ على النار ، وعليها يكون اجتماع الخلائق بأسرهم ، وإِنَّ النار لتفورُ ؛ حتى تعلو من جوانبها ، ويخرج منها أعناق كالجداول تسري بينَ الناسِ فتحملُ مَنْ شَاءَ اللهُ إِلى نفسِها. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « تَقُولُ : وُكُلْتُ بِكُلِّ جَبَّارٍ عَنِيدِ ، وَلَهِيَ أَعْرَفُ بهِمْ مِنَ الْوَالِدَةِ  ِبوَلَدِهَا ، ويكون الذهاب إلى الجنَّةِ على الصراطِ ، ولا سبيل لها إلا عليهِ ، وهو المعني بقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإِن منكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ﴾ [مريم : ٧١).
And among the people of knowledge—and they are the majority—some said: The Sirat is a bridge whose one end is in the land of the Resurrection, and its second end is in the land of Paradise, and it is over the surface of the Fire. And they said: The land of the Resurrection is above the Fire, and upon it will be the gathering of all creatures together. And the Fire will boil until it rises from its sides, and necks like rivers will come out of it, rushing among the people, and they will carry to itself whomever Allah wills. He, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'It says: I have been entrusted with every arrogant tyrant, and it knows them better than a mother knows her child.' And going to Paradise will be upon the Sirat, and there is no way to it except over it. And it is meant by His statement, Exalted: 'And there is none of you but will come to it' (Surah Maryam: 71).
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage presents the second opinion about the nature of the Sirat, held by the majority of scholars. According to this view, the Sirat is a bridge with two ends: one end is on the earth of the Resurrection, where all creatures are gathered, and the other end is in Paradise. The bridge spans over the Fire. The earth of the Resurrection is imagined as a layer above the Fire. The Fire itself is intensely boiling, and from its sides emerge necks (like columns or rivers of fire) that sweep among the people and drag to itself those whom Allah wills. This is supported by a hadith in which the Fire says it is entrusted with every arrogant tyrant, and it recognizes them more intimately than a mother knows her child. The passage then reiterates that the journey to Paradise is only via this Sirat, and it is the referent of the Quranic verse 'And there is none of you but will come to it' (Q. 19:71), indicating that every soul will pass over it.

Misconception: That the Sirat is only a spiritual passage or metaphor.
Correction: The majority opinion affirms the Sirat as a physical bridge with a specific location spanning from the earth of resurrection to Paradise over Hellfire.

Key Takeaway

This lesson reveals that every soul must cross a physical bridge over Hellfire to reach Paradise. Does this reality shape how you view your daily struggles? What is one decision you will make today that reflects the urgency of that crossing?
?
The Sirat is the only way to Paradise. Are you living as if your salvation depends on crossing that bridge? If not, what change must you make in your priorities this week to prepare for that moment?

Four Ways People Enter the Fire
Lists four ways the damned enter Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four distinct ways in which the people of Hell enter the Fire as described in the Quran and transmitted reports.

Core Idea
Hell's inhabitants enter through diverse modes, each emphasizing divine justice.

This passage from Sanusi's creed presents a classification of how the damned enter Hell, drawing from the Quran and prophetic traditions. It lists four distinct methods, each highlighting the variety and power of divine punishment. As you read, notice the vivid imagery—swallowing, snatching, gates, and falling from the bridge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noting the key terms for each category.
Focus on the verbs: تزدرد, تلتقط, يدخل من أبواب, يكب.
2
Identify the four categories
List the four ways mentioned. Notice the parallelism in the structure: 'فمنهم من... ومنهم من...'
3
Reflect on the source
Sanusi cites the Quran and transmitted reports. Consider why he includes this classification in a creed.
It reinforces belief in the unseen and the reality of Hell.
4
Check understanding
Use the checkpoint to test your recall of the four categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ظهرَ مِنْ كتابِ اللهِ سبحانَهُ ومِنْ مأثورِ الأخبارِ : أَنَّ النارَ يدخلُها أهلها على أصناف : فمنهم مَنْ يكون واقفاً على أرض القيامة ، فتزدردُهُ النار وتبتلعُهُ مِنْ موضعِهِ كما يُحْسَفُ بمَنْ يُحْسَفُ على الأَرضِ . ومنهم مَنْ تخرجُ العنقُ مِنَ النارِ فتلتقطهم مِنْ بين الناس إلى نفسها . ومنهم مَنْ يدخلُ مِنْ أبواب النار كما ورد في الكتاب العزيز . ومنهم مَنْ يُكَبُّ مِنَ الصراطِ في النارِ .
Then it appeared from the Book of Allah, Exalted, and from transmitted reports: that the Fire is entered by its people in categories: Among them is one who is standing on the land of the Resurrection, and the Fire swallows him and ingests him from his place, like one who is sunk into the earth. And among them is one for whom a neck emerges from the Fire and snatches them from among the people to itself. And among them is one who enters through the gates of the Fire, as is mentioned in the Mighty Book. And among them is one who is thrown headlong from the Sirat into the Fire.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage classifies the ways in which the people destined for Hell enter it, based on the Quran and transmitted reports. The author lists four distinct categories. The first: some are standing on the land of the Resurrection, and the Fire swallows them up from their very spot, as if the earth itself ingests them. The second: a 'neck' (a column or projection of fire) extends from the Fire and plucks certain people from among the gathered multitude, drawing them into itself. The third: some enter through the gates of the Fire, as described in the Quran—implying that they approach Hell directly through its designated portals. The fourth: some are thrown headfirst from the Sirat (the bridge) into the Fire, presumably because they fall or are cast off during the crossing. The passage does not specify which types of sinners correspond to each category, but it emphasizes the variety of divine punishment.

النار
أرض القيامة
تزدرد
تلتقط
أبواب النار
يكب من الصراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Being swallowed from their place on the land of Resurrection
B) Being snatched by a neck from the Fire
C) Being thrown from the Sirat
D) Being carried by angels on a path of light

Key Takeaway
The Quran and prophetic reports describe four distinct ways the damned enter Hell: being swallowed, snatched by a neck, entering through gates, or thrown from the Sirat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
People are thrown headlong from the Sirat. Imagine standing on that bridge—how firm is your faith? What steps can you take right now to strengthen your footing so that you cross safely?

The Land of Resurrection and the Bridge
Describes the land of Resurrection, the Fire's behavior, and the Bridge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the geography of the Day of Judgment, including the land of Resurrection upon the Fire and the role of the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ) as the only path to Paradise.

Core Idea
The Day of Judgment begins on land over the Fire; Paradise is only reached via the Bridge.

This passage sets the cosmic stage for the events of the Day of Judgment. It describes the land of Resurrection resting upon the Fire itself, with the Fire boiling and sending out 'necks' to snatch the damned. The Prophet (peace be upon him) tells us that the Fire recognizes its tyrants. Then we learn that the only way to Paradise is across the Bridge, which everyone must cross as the Quran says.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the vivid imagery of the Fire boiling and necks like rivers.
2
Focus on the hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) says the Fire declares it has been entrusted with every obstinate tyrant. Reflect on the Fire's ability to recognize its inhabitants.
This hadith highlights the Fire's sentience.
3
Understand the Bridge's role
The passage states that the only way to Paradise is over the Bridge. All creatures must cross it. This is supported by the Quranic verse 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' (Maryam 19:71).
The Bridge is a central feature of the Hereafter.
4
Reflect on the overall scene
Consider how this geography sets the stage for the events to come. The Fire is both beneath the gathering and the destination of the damned.
Think about the purpose of this description in the author's larger argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في أرض القيامةِ ، وطرفُهُ الثاني في أرض الجنَّةِ ، وعلى متن النارِ ، وقالوا : إنَّ أرضَ القيامةِ تكونُ على النار ، وعليها يكون اجتماع الخلائق بأسرهم ، وإِنَّ النار لتفورُ ؛ حتى تعلو من جوانبها ، ويخرج منها أعناق كالجداول تسري بينَ الناسِ فتحملُ مَنْ شَاءَ اللهُ إِلى نفسِها قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « تَقُولُ : وُكِلْتُ بِكُلِّ جَبَّارٍ عَنِيدِ ، وَلَهِيَ أَعْرَفُ بهِمْ مِنَ الْوَالِدَةِ بِوَلَدِهَا (۱) ، ويكون الذهاب إلى الجنَّةِ على الصراطِ ، ولا سبيل لها إلا عليهِ ، وهو المعني بقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإِن منكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ﴾ [مريم : ٧١) . ثم ظهرَ مِنْ كتابِ اللهِ سبحانَهُ ومِنْ مأثورِ الأخبارِ : أَنَّ النارَ يدخلُها أهلها على أصناف : فمنهم مَنْ يكون واقفاً على أرض القيامة ، فتزدردُهُ النار وتبتلعُهُ مِنْ موضعِهِ كما يُحْسَفُ بمَنْ يُحْسَفُ على الأَرضِ . ومنهم مَنْ تخرجُ العنقُ مِنَ النارِ فتلتقطهم مِنْ بين الناس إلى نفسها . ومنهم مَنْ يدخلُ مِنْ أبواب النار كما ورد في الكتاب العزيز . ومنهم مَنْ يُكَبُّ مِنَ الصراطِ في النارِ . (۱) بنحوه في ( المصنف ) لابن أبي شيبة ( ٣٥٣١٥ ) من كلام سيدنا عبد الله بن عمرو رضي الله عنهما ، وبعضه رواه مرفوعاً الترمذي ( ٢٥٧٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه . ومِنْ أهل النارِ مَنْ يُسلَّطُ عليه العطشُ قبل دخولها ، ثم يُرفَعُ لهم سرابٌ يتوهمونَهُ ماءً ، فإذا ذهبوا إليهِ ليشربوا منه كبكبوا في النارِ . وهؤلاء هم أهل الكتاب . وفِرْقةُ يُحال بينهم وبينَ المؤمنينَ ؛ بأنْ يُضرَبَ بينَهم بسورٍ دونَ الجسر ، وهؤلاء هم الشاكونَ المرتابونَ ، وكانوا يصلُّونَ في المساجد ، ويدخلونَ مداخلَ أهلِ الإيمان في معالم الإسلام ، ولذلك : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى وَلَكِنَّكُمْ فَنتُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَتَرَبَّصْتُمْ وَارْتَبْتُمْ وَغَرَّتْكُمُ الْأَمَانِيُّ حَتَّى جَاءَ أَمْرُ اللهِ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ * فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤-١٥] فدل على أنَّهم لم يعبدوا صنماً ، ولكنَّهم كانوا مع المؤمنينَ غيرَ عارفين بما وجب عليهم معرفتُهُ مِنْ أمر الله تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والعياذُ باللهِ مِنَ الاغترار باللهِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ قال تعالى : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] ، وهو الشيطان الرجيم لعنه الله تعالى ؛ يُزينُ لهم ما هم فيه ، ويقولُ لهم : لا حاجة لكم إلى إقامة برهان ، ولا إلى زيادة إيمان وأنتم أهل الجنَّةِ ، فلم يتفقدوا أنفسَهم في شكّها أو في يقينها ، حتى جاءَ أمرُ اللهِ الذي هو الموتُ ، فوجدوا أنفسَهم غير عالمةٍ إِلا بمُجرَّدِ الاعتقادِ ، والتقليد بالآباء والأجداد . وأما المنافقون الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام سراً : فذهبوا معَ مَنْ كانوا يعبدون إلى النار ، ويدخلونَها مِنْ أبوابها ، ويكونون في الدَّرَكِ الأسفلِ مِنَ النارِ .
In the land of the Resurrection, and its other end in the land of Paradise, and upon the surface of the Fire. And they said: The land of the Resurrection is upon the Fire, and upon it is the gathering of all creatures altogether. And indeed the Fire boils until it rises from its sides, and out of it come necks like rivers flowing among the people, carrying whom Allah wills to itself. He, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'It says: I have been entrusted with every tyrant obstinate, and it is more knowledgeable of them than the mother of her child.' And the going to Paradise is upon the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ), and there is no way to it except over it. And it is what is meant by His statement, Exalted: 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' [Maryam 19:71]. Then it became manifest from the Book of Allah, Glorified, and from transmitted reports that the Fire is entered by its people in categories: Among them is one who stands upon the land of the Resurrection, and the Fire swallows him and devours him from his place, as one sinks down into the earth. Among them is one to whom a neck comes out from the Fire and snatches them from among the people to itself. Among them is one who enters through the doors of the Fire as stated in the Mighty Book. Among them is one who is thrown from the Bridge into the Fire. (1) Similarly in (al-Muṣannaf) of Ibn Abī Shayba (35315) from the saying of our master Abdullah ibn Amr, may Allah be pleased with them both, and part of it was narrated as marfūʿ by al-Tirmidhī (2574) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him. And among the people of the Fire are those upon whom thirst is inflicted before entering it, then a mirage is raised for them that they imagine to be water. So when they go to it to drink from it, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are the People of the Book. And a group is separated from the believers by a wall being set between them before the bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics. They used to pray in the mosques and enter the entrances of the people of faith in the landmarks of Islam. Therefore, they call out to them: 'Were we not with you?' They say: 'Yes, but you led yourselves into temptation, and you awaited, and you doubted, and wishful thinking deceived you until the command of Allah came, and the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah.' (Al-Hadid 57:14-15). So it indicates that they did not worship an idol, but they were with the believers without knowing what was obligatory upon them to know of the command of Allah, Exalted, and His Messenger. And we seek refuge in Allah from being deceived by Allah. Indeed He, Exalted, said: 'And the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah' (Al-Hadid 57:14), and he is the accursed devil, may Allah curse him. He beautifies for them what they are in and says to them: You have no need to establish proof or to increase in faith; you are the people of Paradise. So they did not examine themselves regarding their doubt or certainty until the command of Allah, which is death, came. Then they found themselves knowing nothing except mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers. As for the hypocrites who used to worship idols secretly, they go with those they used to worship into the Fire, and they enter it through its doors, and they will be in the lowest depth of the Fire.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a detailed description of the various ways and categories of people who enter the Fire on the Day of Judgment, based on the Quran, hadith, and transmitted reports. It begins by setting the scene: the land of Resurrection is upon the Fire, and the Fire boils, sending out necks like rivers that seize certain people. The Prophet (peace be upon him) is quoted saying that the Fire itself recognizes the tyrants better than a mother knows her child. The passage then notes that entry to Paradise is via the Bridge (al-sirāṭ), and everyone must pass over it, citing the verse 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' (Maryam 19:71). 

Then the author enumerates the categories of people entering the Fire:

1. Those standing on the land of Resurrection who are swallowed by the Fire from their place, like one sinking into the earth.
2. Those snatched by a neck coming from the Fire.
3. Those who enter through the doors of the Fire.
4. Those thrown from the Bridge into the Fire.

After these four categories, the passage discusses additional groups:

- Among the people of the Fire are those who suffer intense thirst before entering; they see a mirage thinking it is water, but when they go to drink, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are identified as the People of the Book (Christians and Jews).

- Another group is separated from the believers by a wall before the Bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics (al-shākkūn al-murtābūn). They outwardly performed Islamic acts like praying in mosques but lacked certain knowledge. They will call out to the believers, and the believers will respond with the Quranic verse from Surah al-Hadid (57:14-15). The passage explains that these people did not worship idols but were ignorant of what was obligatory to know about Allah and His Messenger. They were deceived by Satan (al-gharūr), who made them feel secure without proof or increased faith, so they did not examine their own certainty until death came. They only had blind imitation (taqlīd) of ancestors.

- Finally, the passage mentions the hypocrites (munāfiqūn) who secretly worshipped idols. They will go with those they worshipped into the Fire, entering through its doors and residing in the lowest depth (al-darak al-asfal).

The footnote provides a citation for the hadith about the Fire's statement, attributing it to Ibn Abī Shayba and al-Tirmidhī. The author's purpose is to show the diversity of states among the damned and to warn against mere outward conformity without inner certainty and against being deceived by Satan.

Key Terms

النار
القيامة
الجبار العنيد

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the only way to reach Paradise?
A) Through the land of Resurrection
B) Over the Bridge
C) By entering through the doors of the Fire
D) By being carried by the necks

Key Takeaway
The Fire is the foundation of the Resurrection gathering, and the Bridge is the exclusive path to Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Fire knows the tyrants better than a mother knows her child. Are there hidden tyrants in your heart—pride, envy, or a grudge—that you ignore? Will you confront them today, before that Fire recognizes you?
?
Everyone must cross the Bridge, and there is no other way to Paradise. Is your faith (iman) robust enough to carry you across? What are you relying on besides the mercy of Allah?
?
The Fire boils and sends out necks to seize certain people. If you stood there now, would the Fire's claim over you be for tyranny or for faith? How does that change what you do in the next hour?

The Four Modes of Entering the Fire
Enumerates four ways the damned enter the Fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the four distinct ways the people of the Fire enter it on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The Fire claims its inhabitants in four distinct ways: swallowing, snatching, walking through doors, and falling from the Bridge.

After describing the setting, the author details the various modes of entry into the Fire. These are based on Quranic and transmitted reports. Each mode corresponds to different types of sinners. Understanding these categories helps us appreciate the diversity of divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the four categories
Read the list of four ways the people of the Fire enter. Notice the vivid imagery: being swallowed, snatched by a neck, entering through doors, and being thrown from the Bridge.
Each mode reflects a different type of punishment.
2
Identify each mode
Look at each description: 1) Swallowed from the land, 2) Snatched by a neck, 3) Enter through doors, 4) Thrown from the Bridge.
The footnote is a source citation for the hadith.
3
Reflect on the diversity
Consider why different modes exist. Does the author link them to specific sins? Not explicitly, but the variety shows the Fire actively claims its inhabitants in multiple ways.
Think about how this reinforces the reality of divine punishment.
4
Compare with other groups
Note that this is a general list. Later passages will specify particular groups like the People of the Book and hypocrites.
This sets up the more detailed descriptions to come.

في أرض القيامةِ ، وطرفُهُ الثاني في أرض الجنَّةِ ، وعلى متن النارِ ، وقالوا : إنَّ أرضَ القيامةِ تكونُ على النار ، وعليها يكون اجتماع الخلائق بأسرهم ، وإِنَّ النار لتفورُ ؛ حتى تعلو من جوانبها ، ويخرج منها أعناق كالجداول تسري بينَ الناسِ فتحملُ مَنْ شَاءَ اللهُ إِلى نفسِها قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « تَقُولُ : وُكِلْتُ بِكُلِّ جَبَّارٍ عَنِيدِ ، وَلَهِيَ أَعْرَفُ بهِمْ مِنَ الْوَالِدَةِ بِوَلَدِهَا (۱) ، ويكون الذهاب إلى الجنَّةِ على الصراطِ ، ولا سبيل لها إلا عليهِ ، وهو المعني بقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإِن منكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ﴾ [مريم : ٧١) . ثم ظهرَ مِنْ كتابِ اللهِ سبحانَهُ ومِنْ مأثورِ الأخبارِ : أَنَّ النارَ يدخلُها أهلها على أصناف : فمنهم مَنْ يكون واقفاً على أرض القيامة ، فتزدردُهُ النار وتبتلعُهُ مِنْ موضعِهِ كما يُحْسَفُ بمَنْ يُحْسَفُ على الأَرضِ . ومنهم مَنْ تخرجُ العنقُ مِنَ النارِ فتلتقطهم مِنْ بين الناس إلى نفسها . ومنهم مَنْ يدخلُ مِنْ أبواب النار كما ورد في الكتاب العزيز . ومنهم مَنْ يُكَبُّ مِنَ الصراطِ في النارِ . (۱) بنحوه في ( المصنف ) لابن أبي شيبة ( ٣٥٣١٥ ) من كلام سيدنا عبد الله بن عمرو رضي الله عنهما ، وبعضه رواه مرفوعاً الترمذي ( ٢٥٧٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه . ومِنْ أهل النارِ مَنْ يُسلَّطُ عليه العطشُ قبل دخولها ، ثم يُرفَعُ لهم سرابٌ يتوهمونَهُ ماءً ، فإذا ذهبوا إليهِ ليشربوا منه كبكبوا في النارِ . وهؤلاء هم أهل الكتاب . وفِرْقةُ يُحال بينهم وبينَ المؤمنينَ ؛ بأنْ يُضرَبَ بينَهم بسورٍ دونَ الجسر ، وهؤلاء هم الشاكونَ المرتابونَ ، وكانوا يصلُّونَ في المساجد ، ويدخلونَ مداخلَ أهلِ الإيمان في معالم الإسلام ، ولذلك : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى وَلَكِنَّكُمْ فَنتُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَتَرَبَّصْتُمْ وَارْتَبْتُمْ وَغَرَّتْكُمُ الْأَمَانِيُّ حَتَّى جَاءَ أَمْرُ اللهِ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ * فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤-١٥] فدل على أنَّهم لم يعبدوا صنماً ، ولكنَّهم كانوا مع المؤمنينَ غيرَ عارفين بما وجب عليهم معرفتُهُ مِنْ أمر الله تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والعياذُ باللهِ مِنَ الاغترار باللهِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ قال تعالى : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] ، وهو الشيطان الرجيم لعنه الله تعالى ؛ يُزينُ لهم ما هم فيه ، ويقولُ لهم : لا حاجة لكم إلى إقامة برهان ، ولا إلى زيادة إيمان وأنتم أهل الجنَّةِ ، فلم يتفقدوا أنفسَهم في شكّها أو في يقينها ، حتى جاءَ أمرُ اللهِ الذي هو الموتُ ، فوجدوا أنفسَهم غير عالمةٍ إِلا بمُجرَّدِ الاعتقادِ ، والتقليد بالآباء والأجداد . وأما المنافقون الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام سراً : فذهبوا معَ مَنْ كانوا يعبدون إلى النار ، ويدخلونَها مِنْ أبوابها ، ويكونون في الدَّرَكِ الأسفلِ مِنَ النارِ .
In the land of the Resurrection, and its other end in the land of Paradise, and upon the surface of the Fire. And they said: The land of the Resurrection is upon the Fire, and upon it is the gathering of all creatures altogether. And indeed the Fire boils until it rises from its sides, and out of it come necks like rivers flowing among the people, carrying whom Allah wills to itself. He, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'It says: I have been entrusted with every tyrant obstinate, and it is more knowledgeable of them than the mother of her child.' And the going to Paradise is upon the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ), and there is no way to it except over it. And it is what is meant by His statement, Exalted: 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' [Maryam 19:71]. Then it became manifest from the Book of Allah, Glorified, and from transmitted reports that the Fire is entered by its people in categories: Among them is one who stands upon the land of the Resurrection, and the Fire swallows him and devours him from his place, as one sinks down into the earth. Among them is one to whom a neck comes out from the Fire and snatches them from among the people to itself. Among them is one who enters through the doors of the Fire as stated in the Mighty Book. Among them is one who is thrown from the Bridge into the Fire. (1) Similarly in (al-Muṣannaf) of Ibn Abī Shayba (35315) from the saying of our master Abdullah ibn Amr, may Allah be pleased with them both, and part of it was narrated as marfūʿ by al-Tirmidhī (2574) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him. And among the people of the Fire are those upon whom thirst is inflicted before entering it, then a mirage is raised for them that they imagine to be water. So when they go to it to drink from it, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are the People of the Book. And a group is separated from the believers by a wall being set between them before the bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics. They used to pray in the mosques and enter the entrances of the people of faith in the landmarks of Islam. Therefore, they call out to them: 'Were we not with you?' They say: 'Yes, but you led yourselves into temptation, and you awaited, and you doubted, and wishful thinking deceived you until the command of Allah came, and the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah.' (Al-Hadid 57:14-15). So it indicates that they did not worship an idol, but they were with the believers without knowing what was obligatory upon them to know of the command of Allah, Exalted, and His Messenger. And we seek refuge in Allah from being deceived by Allah. Indeed He, Exalted, said: 'And the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah' (Al-Hadid 57:14), and he is the accursed devil, may Allah curse him. He beautifies for them what they are in and says to them: You have no need to establish proof or to increase in faith; you are the people of Paradise. So they did not examine themselves regarding their doubt or certainty until the command of Allah, which is death, came. Then they found themselves knowing nothing except mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers. As for the hypocrites who used to worship idols secretly, they go with those they used to worship into the Fire, and they enter it through its doors, and they will be in the lowest depth of the Fire.

Which of these is NOT one of the four ways mentioned?
A) Being swallowed

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these four modes of entering the Fire frightens you the most—being swallowed from the ground, snatched by a neck from among the crowd, walking through doors, or falling from the Bridge? What does your fear reveal about your current state of faith and your deeds? Write down one specific action you will take today to avoid that mode.
?
Imagine standing on the land of the Resurrection, knowing that the Fire could open beneath your feet. What sin in your life, if left unrepented, could cause the ground to swallow you? How will you abandon that sin starting now?
?
The Fire has doors, and you might walk through them unknowingly. Which door (e.g., pride, hypocrisy, worldly attachment) do you fear most in yourself? Commit to closing that door today by seeking forgiveness and renewing your intention.

The People of the Book: Thirst and Mirage
Details the specific punishment of the People of the Book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the People of the Book are punished with intense thirst and a deceptive mirage before entering the Fire.

Core Idea
The People of the Book suffer a unique torment: thirst and a mirage that leads them into the Fire.

This passage moves from general categories to a specific group: the People of the Book. Their punishment is distinctive: they are made to suffer unbearable thirst, and then a mirage appears that looks like water, but when they approach to drink, they are tumbled into the Fire. This highlights the fitting nature of their punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the description
Read the short passage about the thirst and mirage. Notice the sequence: thirst, mirage, rushing to drink, and being thrown into the Fire.
The imagery is vivid and symbolic.
2
Identify the group
The passage explicitly says 'These are the People of the Book.' Reflect on why they receive this specific punishment.
The People of the Book are often understood as Christians and Jews.
3
Reflect on the symbolism
Consider how thirst represents their unfulfilled spiritual longing, and the mirage represents false hopes (their corrupted scriptures).
This is a form of poetic justice.
4
Compare with other groups
Note that this is a separate category from the four general modes and the other groups that follow.
It shows a specific fate for a specific type of disbelief.

And indeed the Fire boils until it rises from its sides, and out of it come necks like rivers flowing among the people, carrying whom Allah wills to itself. And the going to Paradise is upon the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ), and there is no way to it except over it. And it is what is meant by His statement, Exalted: 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' [Maryam 19:71]. Then it became manifest from the Book of Allah, Glorified, and from transmitted reports that the Fire is entered by its people in categories: Among them is one who stands upon the land of the Resurrection, and the Fire swallows him and devours him from his place, as one sinks down into the earth. Among them is one to whom a neck comes out from the Fire and snatches them from among the people to itself. Among them is one who enters through the doors of the Fire as stated in the Mighty Book. Among them is one who is thrown from the Bridge into the Fire. (1) Similarly in (al-Muṣannaf) of Ibn Abī Shayba (35315) from the saying of our master Abdullah ibn Amr, may Allah be pleased with them both, and part of it was narrated as marfūʿ by al-Tirmidhī (2574) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him. And among the people of the Fire are those upon whom thirst is inflicted before entering it, then a mirage is raised for them that they imagine to be water. So when they go to it to drink from it, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are the People of the Book. And a group is separated from the believers by a wall being set between them before the bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics. They used to pray in the mosques and enter the entrances of the people of faith in the landmarks of Islam. Therefore, they call out to them: 'Were we not with you?' They say: 'Yes, but you led yourselves into temptation, and you awaited, and you doubted, and wishful thinking deceived you until the command of Allah came, and the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah.' (Al-Hadid 57:14-15). So it indicates that they did not worship an idol, but they were with the believers without knowing what was obligatory upon them to know of the command of Allah, Exalted, and His Messenger. And we seek refuge in Allah from being deceived by Allah. Indeed He, Exalted, said: 'And the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah' (Al-Hadid 57:14), and he is the accursed devil, may Allah curse him. He beautifies for them what they are in and says to them: You have no need to establish proof or to increase in faith; you are the people of Paradise. So they did not examine themselves regarding their doubt or certainty until the command of Allah, which is death, came. Then they found themselves knowing nothing except mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers. As for the hypocrites who used to worship idols secretly, they go with those they used to worship into the Fire, and they enter it through its doors, and they will be in the lowest depth of the Fire.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a detailed description of the various ways and categories of people who enter the Fire on the Day of Judgment, based on the Quran, hadith, and transmitted reports. It begins by setting the scene: the land of Resurrection is upon the Fire, and the Fire boils, sending out necks like rivers that seize certain people. The Prophet (peace be upon him) is quoted saying that the Fire itself recognizes the tyrants better than a mother knows her child. The passage then notes that entry to Paradise is via the Bridge (al-sirāṭ), and everyone must pass over it, citing the verse 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' (Maryam 19:71). 

Then the author enumerates the categories of people entering the Fire:

1. Those standing on the land of Resurrection who are swallowed by the Fire from their place, like one sinking into the earth.
2. Those snatched by a neck coming from the Fire.
3. Those who enter through the doors of the Fire.
4. Those thrown from the Bridge into the Fire.

After these four categories, the passage discusses additional groups:

- Among the people of the Fire are those who suffer intense thirst before entering; they see a mirage thinking it is water, but when they go to drink, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are identified as the People of the Book (Christians and Jews).

- Another group is separated from the believers by a wall before the Bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics (al-shākkūn al-murtābūn). They outwardly performed Islamic acts like praying in mosques but lacked certain knowledge. They will call out to the believers, and the believers will respond with the Quranic verse from Surah al-Hadid (57:14-15). The passage explains that these people did not worship idols but were ignorant of what was obligatory to know about Allah and His Messenger. They were deceived by Satan (al-gharūr), who made them feel secure without proof or increased faith, so they did not examine their own certainty until death came. They only had blind imitation (taqlīd) of ancestors.

- Finally, the passage mentions the hypocrites (munāfiqūn) who secretly worshipped idols. They will go with those they worshipped into the Fire, entering through its doors and residing in the lowest depth (al-darak al-asfal).

The footnote provides a citation for the hadith about the Fire's statement, attributing it to Ibn Abī Shayba and al-Tirmidhī. The author's purpose is to show the diversity of states among the damned and to warn against mere outward conformity without inner certainty and against being deceived by Satan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What affliction do the People of the Book suffer before entering the Fire?
A) Intense cold
B) Intense thirst
C) Being bound in chains
D) Being blind

Key Takeaway
The People of the Book are punished with a thirst that is never satisfied, deceived by a mirage into the Fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever chased something that looked like water but was only a mirage—success, approval, or even religious comfort—that left you more parched than before? The People of the Book ran toward what they thought would quench their thirst, and it threw them into the Fire. What mirage are you running toward right now that might be leading you away from the true source of life?
?
You have the complete scripture, unlike the People of the Book who had only part. But are you truly drinking from it, or are you so absorbed in your own desires that you mistake a mirage for guidance? When will you stop running and ask: 'Am I heading toward water or fire?'
?
The thirst of the People of the Book was a punishment before the punishment. Is there a thirst in your own soul—an unfulfilled longing—that you keep trying to satisfy with illusions? Will you admit today that only Allah can truly quench it, or will you keep stumbling toward the next mirage?

The Doubters and Skeptics: Deceived by Satan
Describes the doubters and skeptics, their separation, and the Quranic rebuke.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fate of the doubters and skeptics—those who outwardly practiced Islam but lacked true certainty—and how they were deceived by Satan.

Core Idea
Doubters who outwardly perform Islamic rites but lack inner certainty are separated from believers and cast into the Fire, deceived by Satan.

This lengthy passage deals with the worst category after outright disbelief: those who prayed and acted like Muslims but harbored doubt and skepticism. They are isolated from the believers by a wall. The passage includes a Quranic dialogue where they admit to having been deceived by wishful thinking and the Deceiver (Satan). The author explains their error: they relied on blind imitation and did not seek true certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the group
Read how they are separated by a wall before the Bridge. Note that they used to pray and engage in Islamic practices.
They are called 'al-shākkūn al-murtābūn' (the doubters and skeptics).
2
Read the Quranic dialogue
Read the verses from Surah al-Hadid (57:14-15) where they call out to the believers and confess their state.
Pay attention to their admission: they were led into temptation, doubted, and were deceived by the Deceiver.
3
Understand the author's explanation
The author clarifies they did not worship idols but were ignorant of necessary knowledge. They relied on mere belief and imitation.
The key phrase: 'they knew nothing except mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers.'
4
Reflect on the role of Satan
Satan (al-Gharūr) beautified their state and told them they had no need for proof or increased faith.
This shows the danger of complacency and blind following.
5
Take the warning to heart
Consider how this applies to one's own faith: the importance of certainty and seeking knowledge.
This is a call to avoid empty ritualism.

(۱) بنحوه في ( المصنف ) لابن أبي شيبة ( ٣٥٣١٥ ) من كلام سيدنا عبد الله بن عمرو رضي الله عنهما ، وبعضه رواه مرفوعاً الترمذي ( ٢٥٧٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه . ومِنْ أهل النارِ مَنْ يُسلَّطُ عليه العطشُ قبل دخولها ، ثم يُرفَعُ لهم سرابٌ يتوهمونَهُ ماءً ، فإذا ذهبوا إليهِ ليشربوا منه كبكبوا في النارِ . وهؤلاء هم أهل الكتاب . وفِرْقةُ يُحال بينهم وبينَ المؤمنينَ ؛ بأنْ يُضرَبَ بينَهم بسورٍ دونَ الجسر ، وهؤلاء هم الشاكونَ المرتابونَ ، وكانوا يصلُّونَ في المساجد ، ويدخلونَ مداخلَ أهلِ الإيمان في معالم الإسلام ، ولذلك : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى وَلَكِنَّكُمْ فَنتُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَتَرَبَّصْتُمْ وَارْتَبْتُمْ وَغَرَّتْكُمُ الْأَمَانِيُّ حَتَّى جَاءَ أَمْرُ اللهِ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ * فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤-١٥] فدل على أنَّهم لم يعبدوا صنماً ، ولكنَّهم كانوا مع المؤمنينَ غيرَ عارفين بما وجب عليهم معرفتُهُ مِنْ أمر الله تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والعياذُ باللهِ مِنَ الاغترار باللهِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ قال تعالى : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] ، وهو الشيطان الرجيم لعنه الله تعالى ؛ يُزينُ لهم ما هم فيه ، ويقولُ لهم : لا حاجة لكم إلى إقامة برهان ، ولا إلى زيادة إيمان وأنتم أهل الجنَّةِ ، فلم يتفقدوا أنفسَهم في شكّها أو في يقينها ، حتى جاءَ أمرُ اللهِ الذي هو الموتُ ، فوجدوا أنفسَهم غير عالمةٍ إِلا بمُجرَّدِ الاعتقادِ ، والتقليد بالآباء والأجداد . وأما المنافقون الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام سراً : فذهبوا معَ مَنْ كانوا يعبدون إلى النار ، ويدخلونَها مِنْ أبوابها ، ويكونون في الدَّرَكِ الأسفلِ مِنَ النارِ .

Commentary
This passage is a detailed description of the various ways and categories of people who enter the Fire on the Day of Judgment, based on the Quran, hadith, and transmitted reports. It begins by setting the scene: the land of Resurrection is upon the Fire, and the Fire boils, sending out necks like rivers that seize certain people. Then the author enumerates the categories of people entering the Fire:

1. Those standing on the land of Resurrection who are swallowed by the Fire from their place, like one sinking into the earth.
2. Those snatched by a neck coming from the Fire.
3. Those who enter through the doors of the Fire.
4. Those thrown from the Bridge into the Fire.

After these four categories, the passage discusses additional groups:

- Among the people of the Fire are those who suffer intense thirst before entering; they see a mirage thinking it is water, but when they go to drink, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are identified as the People of the Book (Christians and Jews).

The author's purpose is to show the diversity of states among the damned and to warn against mere outward conformity without inner certainty and against being deceived by Satan.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Performing Islamic rituals guarantees salvation regardless of inner certainty.

According to the passage, why were the doubters not considered true believers?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray in congregation, do you ever pause to examine whether your heart is truly certain of what you profess, or do you rely on the outward act to deceive yourself into thinking you are safe?
?
What 'wishful thinking' (amānī) has whispered to you that you do not need to seek deeper knowledge of Allah's commands? Will you confront it today?
?
Satan told the doubters they had no need for proof. Whose faith are you living off—your parents', your teacher's, your own? If death came now, would your faith be certain or mere imitation?

The Hypocrites: Lowest Depth of the Fire
States the punishment of hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the fate of the hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols—they will enter the Fire through its doors and reside in its lowest depth.

Core Idea
Hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols are cast into the lowest depth of the Fire.

The final group mentioned in this passage is the true hypocrites (munāfiqūn), who hid their idol worship. Their punishment is the worst: they enter through the doors of the Fire and are placed in the lowest depth (al-darak al-asfal). This shows that internal hypocrisy carries the severest penalty.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the sentence about the hypocrites. It is brief but packed with meaning.
Notice the contrast with the doubters.
2
Understand their crime
They secretly worshipped idols while outwardly appearing as Muslims. This is a double betrayal.
They are the worst of the worst.
3
Note their destination
They go with the idols they worshipped into the Fire and are placed in the lowest depth (al-darak al-asfal).
The lowest depth is the most severe part of Hell.
4
Compare with other groups
Contrast with the doubters who did not worship idols but lacked knowledge. The hypocrites intentionally deceived.
This shows gradation in punishment.

(۱) بنحوه في ( المصنف ) لابن أبي شيبة ( ٣٥٣١٥ ) من كلام سيدنا عبد الله بن عمرو رضي الله عنهما ، وبعضه رواه مرفوعاً الترمذي ( ٢٥٧٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه . ومِنْ أهل النارِ مَنْ يُسلَّطُ عليه العطشُ قبل دخولها ، ثم يُرفَعُ لهم سرابٌ يتوهمونَهُ ماءً ، فإذا ذهبوا إليهِ ليشربوا منه كبكبوا في النارِ . وهؤلاء هم أهل الكتاب . وفِرْقةُ يُحال بينهم وبينَ المؤمنينَ ؛ بأنْ يُضرَبَ بينَهم بسورٍ دونَ الجسر ، وهؤلاء هم الشاكونَ المرتابونَ ، وكانوا يصلُّونَ في المساجد ، ويدخلونَ مداخلَ أهلِ الإيمان في معالم الإسلام ، ولذلك : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى وَلَكِنَّكُمْ فَنتُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَتَرَبَّصْتُمْ وَارْتَبْتُمْ وَغَرَّتْكُمُ الْأَمَانِيُّ حَتَّى جَاءَ أَمْرُ اللهِ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ * فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤-١٥] فدل على أنَّهم لم يعبدوا صنماً ، ولكنَّهم كانوا مع المؤمنينَ غيرَ عارفين بما وجب عليهم معرفتُهُ مِنْ أمر الله تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والعياذُ باللهِ مِنَ الاغترار باللهِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ قال تعالى : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] ، وهو الشيطان الرجيم لعنه الله تعالى ؛ يُزينُ لهم ما هم فيه ، ويقولُ لهم : لا حاجة لكم إلى إقامة برهان ، ولا إلى زيادة إيمان وأنتم أهل الجنَّةِ ، فلم يتفقدوا أنفسَهم في شكّها أو في يقينها ، حتى جاءَ أمرُ اللهِ الذي هو الموتُ ، فوجدوا أنفسَهم غير عالمةٍ إِلا بمُجرَّدِ الاعتقادِ ، والتقليد بالآباء والأجداد . وأما المنافقون الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام سراً : فذهبوا معَ مَنْ كانوا يعبدون إلى النار ، ويدخلونَها مِنْ أبوابها ، ويكونون في الدَّرَكِ الأسفلِ مِنَ النارِ .
In the land of the Resurrection, and its other end in the land of Paradise, and upon the surface of the Fire. And they said: The land of the Resurrection is upon the Fire, and upon it is the gathering of all creatures altogether. And indeed the Fire boils until it rises from its sides, and out of it come necks like rivers flowing among the people, carrying whom Allah wills to itself. He, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'It says: I have been entrusted with every tyrant obstinate, and it is more knowledgeable of them than the mother of her child.' And the going to Paradise is upon the Bridge (al-ṣirāṭ), and there is no way to it except over it. And it is what is meant by His statement, Exalted: 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' [Maryam 19:71]. Then it became manifest from the Book of Allah, Glorified, and from transmitted reports that the Fire is entered by its people in categories: Among them is one who stands upon the land of the Resurrection, and the Fire swallows him and devours him from his place, as one sinks down into the earth. Among them is one to whom a neck comes out from the Fire and snatches them from among the people to itself. Among them is one who enters through the doors of the Fire as stated in the Mighty Book. Among them is one who is thrown from the Bridge into the Fire. (1) Similarly in (al-Muṣannaf) of Ibn Abī Shayba (35315) from the saying of our master Abdullah ibn Amr, may Allah be pleased with them both, and part of it was narrated as marfūʿ by al-Tirmidhī (2574) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him. And among the people of the Fire are those upon whom thirst is inflicted before entering it, then a mirage is raised for them that they imagine to be water. So when they go to it to drink from it, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are the People of the Book. And a group is separated from the believers by a wall being set between them before the bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics. They used to pray in the mosques and enter the entrances of the people of faith in the landmarks of Islam. Therefore, they call out to them: 'Were we not with you?' They say: 'Yes, but you led yourselves into temptation, and you awaited, and you doubted, and wishful thinking deceived you until the command of Allah came, and the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah.' (Al-Hadid 57:14-15). So it indicates that they did not worship an idol, but they were with the believers without knowing what was obligatory upon them to know of the command of Allah, Exalted, and His Messenger. And we seek refuge in Allah from being deceived by Allah. Indeed He, Exalted, said: 'And the Deceiver deceived you concerning Allah' (Al-Hadid 57:14), and he is the accursed devil, may Allah curse him. He beautifies for them what they are in and says to them: You have no need to establish proof or to increase in faith; you are the people of Paradise. So they did not examine themselves regarding their doubt or certainty until the command of Allah, which is death, came. Then they found themselves knowing nothing except mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers. As for the hypocrites who used to worship idols secretly, they go with those they used to worship into the Fire, and they enter it through its doors, and they will be in the lowest depth of the Fire.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a detailed description of the various ways and categories of people who enter the Fire on the Day of Judgment, based on the Quran, hadith, and transmitted reports. It begins by setting the scene: the land of Resurrection is upon the Fire, and the Fire boils, sending out necks like rivers that seize certain people. The Prophet (peace be upon him) is quoted saying that the Fire itself recognizes the tyrants better than a mother knows her child. The passage then notes that entry to Paradise is via the Bridge (al-sirāṭ), and everyone must pass over it, citing the verse 'And there is none of you except that he will come to it' (Maryam 19:71). 

Then the author enumerates the categories of people entering the Fire:

1. Those standing on the land of Resurrection who are swallowed by the Fire from their place, like one sinking into the earth.
2. Those snatched by a neck coming from the Fire.
3. Those who enter through the doors of the Fire.
4. Those thrown from the Bridge into the Fire.

After these four categories, the passage discusses additional groups:

- Among the people of the Fire are those who suffer intense thirst before entering; they see a mirage thinking it is water, but when they go to drink, they are tumbled into the Fire. These are identified as the People of the Book (Christians and Jews).

- Another group is separated from the believers by a wall before the Bridge. These are the doubters and skeptics (al-shākkūn al-murtābūn). They outwardly performed Islamic acts like praying in mosques but lacked certain knowledge. They will call out to the believers, and the believers will respond with the Quranic verse from Surah al-Hadid (57:14-15). The passage explains that these people did not worship idols but were ignorant of what was obligatory to know about Allah and His Messenger. They were deceived by Satan (al-gharūr), who made them feel secure without proof or increased faith, so they did not examine their own certainty until death came. They only had blind imitation (taqlīd) of ancestors.

- Finally, the passage mentions the hypocrites (munāfiqūn) who secretly worshipped idols. They will go with those they worshipped into the Fire, entering through its doors and residing in the lowest depth (al-darak al-asfal).

The footnote provides a citation for the hadith about the Fire's statement, attributing it to Ibn Abī Shayba and al-Tirmidhī. The author's purpose is to show the diversity of states among the damned and to warn against mere outward conformity without inner certainty and against being deceived by Satan.

الأصنام
الدَّرَك الأسفل

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever hidden a sin or doubt in your heart while appearing righteous to others? How does knowing that the lowest depth of Hell is specifically for such hypocrisy change your view of your own hidden faults? What step will you take today to bring a secret issue before Allah in sincere repentance?
?
If you knew that every secret thought of shirk or doubt is recorded and will be exposed and punished according to its reality, how would you guard your inner state? What specific empty or false belief are you tempted to harbor secretly? Will you confront it now?
?
The passage says hypocrites go with those they worshipped into the Fire. What or who are you most afraid of losing? Could that fear be a form of hidden shirk? Be honest: is there anything you love more than Allah to the point that you would hide it? What will you do about it before it leads you to the lowest depth?

The Thirst Group: People of the Book on the Day of Judgment
Sanusi describes the punishment of a group from the People of the Book who suffer thirst and are tricked by a mirage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the punishment of a specific group from the People of the Book who suffer intense thirst and are deceived by a mirage before entering Hell.

Core Idea
Thirst and mirage — a unique punishment for those who had Scripture but did not believe.

Sanusi begins by describing a special punishment for a group from the People of the Book. They are not the same as open disbelievers; rather, they had Scripture but failed to accept the truth. Their torment begins with intense thirst, followed by a deceptive mirage that leads them into the Fire.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage about the thirst group. Note the sequence: thirst, mirage, attempt to drink, then tumbled into Fire.
The word 'دون' may indicate an exception, but the meaning is unclear.
2
Identify the group
Recognize that the group is identified as 'أهل الكتاب' (People of the Book). Consider why they might receive this unique punishment.
3
Reflect on the symbolism
The mirage symbolizes false hope. Just as they were deceived in this world by their scripture without true faith, they are deceived by a mirage in the afterlife.
This connects their worldly delusion to their punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومِنْ أهل النارِ مَنْ يُسلَّطُ عليه العطشُ قبل دخولها ، ثم يُرفَعُ لهم سرابٌ يتوهمونَهُ ماءً ، فإذا ذهبوا إليهِ ليشربوا منه كبكبوا في النارِ وهؤلاء هم أهل الكتاب دون وفِرْقةُ يُحال بينهم وبينَ المؤمنينَ ؛ بأنْ يُضرَبَ بينَهم بسورٍ الجسر ، وهؤلاء هم الشاكونَ المرتابونَ ، وكانوا يصلُّونَ في المساجد ، ويدخلونَ مداخلَ أهلِ الإيمان في معالم الإسلام ، ولذلك : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى وَلَكِنَّكُمْ فَتَنْتُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَتَرَبَّصْتُمْ وَارْتَبْتُمْ وَغَرَّتْكُمُ الْأَمَانِيُّ حَتَّى جَاءَ أَمْرُ اللهِ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ * فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤-١٥] فدل على أنَّهم لم يعبدوا صنماً ، ولكنَّهم كانوا مع المؤمنينَ غيرَ عارفين بما وجب عليهم معرفتُهُ مِنْ أمر الله تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والعياذُ باللهِ مِنَ الاغترار باللهِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ قال تعالى : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] ، وهو الشيطان الرجيم لعنه الله تعالى ؛ يُزينُ لهم ما هم فيه ، ويقولُ لهم : لا حاجة لكم إلى إقامة برهان ، ولا إلى زيادة إيمان وأنتم أهل الجنَّةِ ، فلم يتفقدوا أنفسَهم في شكّها أو في يقينها ، حتى جاءَ أمرُ اللهِ الذي هو الموتُ ، فوجدوا أنفسَهم غير عالمةٍ إِلا بمُجرَّدِ الاعتقادِ ، والتقليد بالآباء والأجداد وأما المنافقون الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام سراً : فذهبوا معَ مَنْ كانوا يعبدون إلى النار ، ويدخلونَها مِنْ أبوابها ، ويكونون في الدَّرَكِ الأسفلِ مِنَ النارِ وأما الطائفةُ التي لا بدَّ أنْ تخرجَ مِنَ النارِ - وهم أصحابُ الكبائرِ مِنْ أهل الإيمان - : فيكونون على الصراط كل على حسبِ تقصيره في أمرِ دينه يكون بطؤُهُ على الصراطِ ، قالَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : « حَتَّى يَقُولَ الْعَبْدُ : يَا رَبِّ ؛ أَبْطَأْتَ بِي ، فَيَقُولُ لَهُ : أَبْطَأَ بِكَ عَمَلُكَ » ) انتهى منهم
And among the people of the Fire are those who are made to suffer thirst before entering it, then a mirage is raised for them which they imagine to be water, so when they go to it to drink from it, they are tumbled back into the Fire. These are the People of the Book except for (?) and a group is barred between them and the believers, by a wall being struck between them, the bridge (al-jisr). These are the doubters, the sceptics. They used to pray in the mosques and enter the entrances of the people of faith in the landmarks of Islam. Therefore, they are called out: 'Were we not with you?' They say: 'Yes, but you tempted yourselves, and waited, and doubted, and wishes deluded you until the command of Allah came, and the Deceiver deluded you concerning Allah.' So today no ransom shall be taken from you nor from those who disbelieved (Surah al-Hadid 14-15). So this indicates that they did not worship an idol, but they were with the believers, not knowing what was obligatory upon them to know of the matter of Allah Most High and His Messenger. And refuge is sought with Allah from being deluded by Allah; for He Most High said: 'And the Deceiver deluded you concerning Allah' (Surah al-Hadid 14), and he is the accursed devil; Allah curse him. He beautifies for them what they are in, and says to them: 'You have no need to establish a proof, nor to increase faith, and you are the people of Paradise.' So they did not examine themselves regarding their doubt or their certainty, until the command of Allah, which is death, came, and they found themselves knowing only by mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers. And as for the hypocrites who used to worship idols secretly, they went with those they worshipped to the Fire, and enter it through its doors, and they shall be in the lowest depth of the Fire. And as for the group that must eventually leave the Fire – and they are the people of major sins from the people of faith – they will be upon the Ṣirāṭ, each according to his negligence in matters of his religion will be his slowness on the Ṣirāṭ. The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Until the servant says: O Lord, You have slowed me down, so He says to him: Your deed slowed you down.' End of their [description].
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage describes the fates of three distinct groups on the Day of Judgment: (1) A group of the people of the Fire who are made intensely thirsty before entering Hell. They see a mirage they think is water, but when they go to drink, they are cast into the Fire. These are said to be the People of the Book (with an unclear exception). (2) A group separated from the believers by a wall (the Bridge, jisr). They are the sceptics who outwardly practiced Islam—praying in mosques and joining believers—but inwardly doubted. The Quranic verse (al-Hadid 14-15) shows that they did not commit idolatry but lacked true knowledge of Allah and His Messenger. They were deluded by Satan into thinking they were safe without proof. Thus, at death, they had only blind imitation. (3) The hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols go with their idols to the lowest depth of Hell. Then the passage turns to the group that will eventually exit the Fire—the grave sinners from the believers. They cross the Ṣirāṭ (bridge over Hell) with slowness proportional to their sins. The Prophet's hadith confirms that a person's deeds determine their speed on the Ṣirāṭ. The phrase 'End of their [description]' likely closes the discussion of these groups.

السراب
أهل الكتاب

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have been given the Quran, a clear scripture. Yet, are there areas in your life where you treat Allah's guidance like a mirage—acknowledging it intellectually but acting as if it is not real? What is one step you will take today to transform knowledge into action before the thirst of regret overtakes you?
?
Imagine standing on the Plain of Judgment, parched with a thirst that no water can quench, and seeing a shimmering hope that turns out to be a deception. What worldly hope are you clutching right now that might be a mirage? Will you abandon it for the true water of Islam, or will you cling to it until it casts you into the Fire?
?
The People of the Book had scriptures but were damned by their choices. You have the Qur'an in your hands. If you were to die tonight, would your relationship with Allah be based on a mirage of self-satisfaction, or would it be the real thing? What will you change starting now?

The Sceptics: Outward Muslims Who Doubted
Sanusi describes the sceptics who outwardly practiced Islam but doubted, and their separation from the believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition of those who outwardly practiced Islam but inwardly doubted, and how they are separated from the believers on Judgment Day.

Core Idea
Outward practice without inward certainty leads to separation from the believers on Judgment Day.

Sanusi now turns to a group that appeared to be Muslims—they prayed in mosques and followed Islamic practices—but they were sceptics and doubters. They are separated from the believers by a wall (the Bridge). Their fate is revealed in the Quranic verse from Surah al-Hadid, which shows that their punishment is due to delusion and blind imitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group
The passage calls them 'الشاكون المرتابون' (the doubters, the sceptics). Note their outward actions: they prayed in mosques and mixed with believers.
2
Understand their inner state
They had doubt in their hearts. They were deluded by Satan into thinking they had no need for proof or deeper faith.
The Quranic verse shows their admission: 'ألم نكن معكم' they say yes but were deluded.
3
Recognize the danger of blind imitation
They only had mere belief and imitation of ancestors, not certain knowledge. This is why they are separated.
This warns against accepting faith without understanding.

ومِنْ أهل النارِ مَنْ يُسلَّطُ عليه العطشُ قبل دخولها ، ثم يُرفَعُ لهم سرابٌ يتوهمونَهُ ماءً ، فإذا ذهبوا إليهِ ليشربوا منه كبكبوا في النارِ وهؤلاء هم أهل الكتاب دون وفِرْقةُ يُحال بينهم وبينَ المؤمنينَ ؛ بأنْ يُضرَبَ بينَهم بسورٍ الجسر ، وهؤلاء هم الشاكونَ المرتابونَ ، وكانوا يصلُّونَ في المساجد ، ويدخلونَ مداخلَ أهلِ الإيمان في معالم الإسلام ، ولذلك : يُنَادُونَهُمْ أَلَمْ تَكُن مَّعَكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى وَلَكِنَّكُمْ فَتَنْتُمْ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَتَرَبَّصْتُمْ وَارْتَبْتُمْ وَغَرَّتْكُمُ الْأَمَانِيُّ حَتَّى جَاءَ أَمْرُ اللهِ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ * فَالْيَوْمَ لَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنكُمْ فِدْيَةٌ وَلَا مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤-١٥] فدل على أنَّهم لم يعبدوا صنماً ، ولكنَّهم كانوا مع المؤمنينَ غيرَ عارفين بما وجب عليهم معرفتُهُ مِنْ أمر الله تعالى ورسولِهِ ، والعياذُ باللهِ مِنَ الاغترار باللهِ ؛ فإِنَّهُ قال تعالى : ﴿ وَغَرَّكُم بِاللَّهِ الْغَرُورُ ﴾ [الحديد : ١٤] ، وهو الشيطان الرجيم لعنه الله تعالى ؛ يُزينُ لهم ما هم فيه ، ويقولُ لهم : لا حاجة لكم إلى إقامة برهان ، ولا إلى زيادة إيمان وأنتم أهل الجنَّةِ ، فلم يتفقدوا أنفسَهم في شكّها أو في يقينها ، حتى جاءَ أمرُ اللهِ الذي هو الموتُ ، فوجدوا أنفسَهم غير عالمةٍ إِلا بمُجرَّدِ الاعتقادِ ، والتقليد بالآباء والأجداد وأما المنافقون الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام سراً : فذهبوا معَ مَنْ كانوا يعبدون إلى النار ، ويدخلونَها مِنْ أبوابها ، ويكونون في الدَّرَكِ الأسفلِ مِنَ النارِ وأما الطائفةُ التي لا بدَّ أنْ تخرجَ مِنَ النارِ - وهم أصحابُ الكبائرِ مِنْ أهل الإيمان - : فيكونون على الصراط كل على حسبِ تقصيره في أمرِ دينه يكون بطؤُهُ على الصراطِ ، قالَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : « حَتَّى يَقُولَ الْعَبْدُ : يَا رَبِّ ؛ أَبْطَأْتَ بِي ، فَيَقُولُ لَهُ : أَبْطَأَ بِكَ عَمَلُكَ » ) انتهى منهم
And among the people of the Fire are those who are made to suffer thirst before entering it, then a mirage is raised for them which they imagine to be water, so when they go to it to drink from it, they are tumbled back into the Fire. These are the People of the Book except for (?) and a group is barred between them and the believers, by a wall being struck between them, the bridge (al-jisr). These are the doubters, the sceptics. They used to pray in the mosques and enter the entrances of the people of faith in the landmarks of Islam. Therefore, they are called out: 'Were we not with you?' They say: 'Yes, but you tempted yourselves, and waited, and doubted, and wishes deluded you until the command of Allah came, and the Deceiver deluded you concerning Allah.' So today no ransom shall be taken from you nor from those who disbelieved (Surah al-Hadid 14-15). So this indicates that they did not worship an idol, but they were with the believers, not knowing what was obligatory upon them to know of the matter of Allah Most High and His Messenger. And refuge is sought with Allah from being deluded by Allah; for He Most High said: 'And the Deceiver deluded you concerning Allah' (Surah al-Hadid 14), and he is the accursed devil; Allah curse him. He beautifies for them what they are in, and says to them: 'You have no need to establish a proof, nor to increase faith, and you are the people of Paradise.' So they did not examine themselves regarding their doubt or their certainty, until the command of Allah, which is death, came, and they found themselves knowing only by mere belief and imitation of fathers and forefathers. And as for the hypocrites who used to worship idols secretly, they went with those they worshipped to the Fire, and enter it through its doors, and they shall be in the lowest depth of the Fire. And as for the group that must eventually leave the Fire – and they are the people of major sins from the people of faith – they will be upon the Ṣirāṭ, each according to his negligence in matters of his religion will be his slowness on the Ṣirāṭ. The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Until the servant says: O Lord, You have slowed me down, so He says to him: Your deed slowed you down.' End of their [description].
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage describes the fates of three distinct groups on the Day of Judgment: (1) A group of the people of the Fire who are made intensely thirsty before entering Hell. They see a mirage they think is water, but when they go to drink, they are cast into the Fire. These are said to be the People of the Book (with an unclear exception). (2) A group separated from the believers by a wall (the Bridge, jisr). They are the sceptics who outwardly practiced Islam—praying in mosques and joining believers—but inwardly doubted. The Quranic verse (al-Hadid 14-15) shows that they did not commit idolatry but lacked true knowledge of Allah and His Messenger. They were deluded by Satan into thinking they were safe without proof. Thus, at death, they had only blind imitation. (3) The hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols go with their idols to the lowest depth of Hell. Then the passage turns to the group that will eventually exit the Fire—the grave sinners from the believers. They cross the Ṣirāṭ (bridge over Hell) with slowness proportional to their sins. The Prophet's hadith confirms that a person's deeds determine their speed on the Ṣirāṭ. The phrase 'End of their [description]' likely closes the discussion of these groups.

Key Terms
الجسر
الشاكون المرتابون
الاغترار
التقليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the attitude of the sceptics towards religious knowledge according to Sanusi?
A) They sought proofs and increased their faith
B) They imitated their fathers without understanding
C) They rejected all forms of worship
D) They were secretly idolaters

Key Takeaway
Sceptics who doubt while outwardly practicing Islam will be separated from the believers on the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever performed an act of worship mechanically while your heart was filled with doubt or indifference? What would it take for you to seek certainty from this lesson today?
?
You may have relied on the faith of your parents or community your whole life—but if you were to stand before Allah right now, would your own ma'rifah of Him be enough to save you from the separation described here?
?
Satan deceives the sceptics into thinking they are safe without proof. Where in your life have you assumed that outward practice alone guarantees Paradise? Will you now commit to seeking deep certainty over shallow conformity?

The Hypocrites: Secret Idol Worshippers
Sanusi gives the fate of hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fate of the hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols while appearing Muslim.

Core Idea
Hypocrites who hide their disbelief go to the lowest depth of Hell with their idols.

Sanusi then describes the hypocrites—those who professed Islam but secretly worshipped idols. Their punishment is to enter Hell with their idols and be placed in the lowest depth. This shows that hidden disbelief is worse than open doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
The passage is very short: hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols go with them into Hell.
2
Understand the term
Here 'المنافقون' specifically denotes those who hid idol worship, not the common definition of hypocrisy.
3
Note the severity
They enter from the doors of Hell and go to the lowest depth (الدرك الأسفل), indicating the worst punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever concealed a belief or action that contradicts your outward Islam? What is stopping you from repenting and making it public to Allah today?
?

?
If your inner state were exposed right now, would you still be among the truthful believers? What one concrete step will you take this week to align your heart with your tongue?

Unseen Matters
intermediate
4 min
Grave Sinners on the Ṣirāṭ
Sanusi describes the crossing of the Ṣirāṭ by grave sinners from Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the grave sinners from the people of faith cross the Ṣirāṭ and that their speed depends on their deeds.

Core Idea
On the Ṣirāṭ, believers with major sins cross slowly according to their negligence; their deeds determine their pace.

Finally, Sanusi discusses the group that will eventually exit Hell—the people of major sins from the believers. They will cross the Ṣirāṭ (the bridge over Hell), and their slowness on it corresponds to their negligence in religious duties. A hadith of the Prophet confirms that a person's deeds cause their slowness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group
These are the people of major sins (أصحاب الكبائر) from the people of faith (أهل الإيمان), who will ultimately leave Hell.
2
Understand the Ṣirāṭ
The Ṣirāṭ is a bridge over Hell that everyone must cross. Speed on it is proportional to one's deeds.
The hadith illustrates this: the servant says 'أبطأت بي' and is told 'أبطأ بك عملك'.
3
Reflect on personal accountability
This shows that even for believers, salvation is not automatic; sins cause delay and require purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Quranic verse (al-Hadid 14-15) shows that they did not commit idolatry but lacked true knowledge of Allah and His Messenger. They were deluded by Satan into thinking they were safe without proof. Thus, at death, they had only blind imitation. (3) The hypocrites who secretly worshipped idols go with their idols to the lowest depth of Hell. Then the passage turns to the group that will eventually exit the Fire—the grave sinners from the believers. They cross the Ṣirāṭ (bridge over Hell) with slowness proportional to their sins. The Prophet's hadith confirms that a person's deeds determine their speed on the Ṣirāṭ. The phrase 'End of their [description]' likely closes the discussion of these groups.

الكبائر
أبطأ به عمله

Key Takeaway
On the Ṣirāṭ, believers with major sins cross slowly; their deeds cause their delay.

?

?

?
When you face hardship, do you tend to blame Allah or circumstances? How can you instead examine your own actions and take responsibility, as the hadith teaches?

Refutation of Mu'tazilite Denial of the Ṣirāṭ
Refutation of Mu'tazilite denial of the Ṣirāṭ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite rejection of the literal Ṣirāṭ, their alternative interpretations, and the Sunni response affirming its literal reality based on divine omnipotence and scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
The Ṣirāṭ is real and possible because what is impossible for man is easy for Allah.

The Mu'tazilites, driven by rational considerations, denied the literal bridge over Hell and proposed various metaphorical interpretations. Sanusi refutes them by affirming divine power and citing textual support, reminding us that the hereafter is not bound by worldly physical laws.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite objection
Read the first part of the passage where the Mu'tazilites give two reasons for rejecting a literal Ṣirāṭ: impossibility of crossing and the inappropriateness of punishing believers on that day.
Notice that they focus on rational impossibility and theological appropriateness.
2
Examine their alternative interpretations
Identify the four alternative interpretations of the Ṣirāṭ proposed by different Mu'tazilite groups: as the path to Paradise/Fire, as clear proofs, as acts of worship, or as evil deeds whose crossing varies in length.
These show how they try to reconcile the scriptural term with their rational framework.
3
Analyze the Sunni answer
Read the brief answer: crossing is possible like walking on water, referring to divine power and a supporting hadith. Consider how this refutes the rational objection.
The answer relies on God's ability to suspend natural laws, akin to miracles.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
Contemplate the lesson's core idea: divine omnipotence overrides human rational objections when it comes to eschatological realities.
This is a key difference between Sunnis and Mu'tazilites in theological method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And many of the Mu'tazilites denied that the Ṣirāṭ is upon its apparent meaning, claiming that crossing it is not possible, and if it were possible then it would involve punishment, and there is no punishment for the believers and the righteous on the Day of Resurrection. They said: Rather, what is meant by the Ṣirāṭ is the path to Paradise, indicated by His Most High statement: 'He will guide them and set right their condition' (Surah Muhammad 5), and the path to the Fire, indicated by His Most High statement: 'Then guide them to the path of Hellfire' (Surah as-Saffat 23). And among them are those who interpreted it as the clear proofs. And among them are those who interpreted it as acts of worship, like prayer, zakah, and the like. And among them are those who interpreted it as the evil deeds which one is asked about and taken to account for, as if he passed over them, and the crossing lengthens with their abundance and shortens with their scarcity. And the answer: That the possibility of crossing is apparent, like walking on water. (1) See 'Nukat al-Irshad' (4) 202-203, and the hadith: 'Until the servant says: O Lord, You have slowed me down, so He says to him: Your deed delayed you...' to the end, it is a piece of a long hadith narrated by al-Tabarani in al-Mu'jam al-Kabir (9/354) and al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak (4/496) from the hadith of our master Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage presents a Mu'tazilite objection and the answer to it. The Mu'tazilites reject the literal interpretation of the Ṣirāṭ (the bridge over Hell) for two reasons: (1) they claim crossing is impossible, and (2) even if possible, it would constitute punishment for believers and righteous people, which they think is unfitting on the Day of Resurrection. They propose alternative interpretations: that the Ṣirāṭ is the path to Paradise or Hell, or the clear proofs of religion, or acts of worship (like prayer and zakah), or a metaphor for evil deeds whose crossing becomes long or short depending on one's sins. The answer to this is brief but decisive: crossing the Ṣirāṭ is possible, just as walking on water is possible by divine power. The author then references a source (Nukat al-Irshad) and a prophetic hadith supporting the literal Ṣirāṭ. This refutes the Mu'tazilite rational objection by appealing to divine omnipotence and textual evidence.
